However, the main reason for Zhao Dexiong's suicide was not just this one incident. The Zhenxing Yarn Mill was under environmental pressure and had mortgaged the factory to the Hui Deng Bank to borrow foreign capital and maintain its precarious situation. When Zhao Dexiong's last desperate gamble also failed, the bank's comprador forced him to sign a contract to transfer the factory. Dexiong suffered this major blow and went mad.

Observing the above situation, the changes in the battle between golden women are vividly depicted, and the oppression of national capital by international capital is also clarified. If this theme were used to create a movie script, it would be thought-provoking and serve as a wake-up call to analyze the reasons for industrial and commercial decline. The new sound film "Hero of the Times" by Yihua Film Company adopts the above theme and adds various technical advancements, undoubtedly making it a masterpiece of domestic films. The director is Mr. Ying Yunwei, and the leading actors include Hu Ping, Shang Guanwu, Wang Naidong, Ma Loufen, Ye Juanjuan, Wan Laitian, and other major stars. It will be officially released at the Jincheng Grand Theater in the coming days, and people from all walks of life are urged to pay special attention.

After Gan Weilu Restored Chinese Nationality, He Refused to Pay the Municipal Council's House Tax: Detailed Ten Reasons Based on Law and Fact, Requesting the Court to Make a Fair Judgment on Unequal Rights and Obligations 151

The Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council collects taxes from residents within the concession based on the amount of rent paid by the residents, and collects 14% of the rent monthly. For example, if the monthly rent is 100 yuan, the tax is 14 yuan, which is collected by the council in four seasons. If there are any arrears, the council will sue in the First Special District Court according to law. All residents, Chinese and foreign, are treated equally without any favoritism. Now there is a Cantonese lawyer, Gan Deyun, who was also a lawyer in Shanghai during the time of the Mixed Court. However, his name was Gan Weilu, and his nationality was English. He had the obligation to pay taxes to the Municipal Council. However, Gan always attended the annual taxpayers' meeting and enjoyed the right to vote. In recent years, he has restored his Chinese nationality, and this voting right has been revoked. Therefore, he is unwilling to bear the obligation to pay taxes. From April 1 of this year to the end of the year, he owes a total of 239.40 yuan for the summer, autumn, and winter taxes, which the council has repeatedly sent people to collect from his office at 505 Henan Road, but he still refuses to pay. The council has recently sued him in the First Special Court, requesting that he be ordered to pay the full amount and bear the litigation costs. After being sued, Gan filed a statement of defense, listing ten reasons why the Municipal Council has no right to collect taxes from him, saying what others cannot say. His words are roughly as follows: (1) The plaintiff is a foreign municipal organization, and its exercise of power in Chinese territory without the approval and permission of the government of the Republic of China is illegal. (2) The plaintiff has no right to collect taxes from the defendant, nor can it sue the defendant. (3) The plaintiff cannot clearly state the origin of its power to collect taxes from Chinese people. (4) The right to vote and the knowledge of the collection and payment of taxes are universally recognized by taxpayers. (5) The reason why the defendant does not pay house tax is that he cannot obtain the right to vote at the annual taxpayers' meeting, while Westerners who pay the same amount of tax can attend and vote. (6) The defendant is unwilling to pay the tax because of the plaintiff's discriminatory attitude, which is too unfair. (7) According to which law does the Municipal Council only allow Westerners to vote and exclude Chinese people from enjoying the same rights? (8) The former Qing government did not grant the Shanghai Public Concession the right to collect taxes from Chinese people. (9) 14% of the house tax is too high, illegal, and has not been agreed to by the defendant. (10) If the defendant can obtain the right to vote, he is also willing to pay fair and reasonable taxes. At the end of the statement, it is stated that the total number of Chinese taxpayers in the Public Concession reaches 75% of the total population, but they have no right to elect members at the annual meeting. The tax principles of all civilized countries in the world universally recognize that the right to representation is the counterpart of the obligation to pay taxes. Therefore, before Chinese people can enjoy the same rights as Westerners, they cannot recognize the payment of this tax, and request the court to make a fair judgment, dismiss the plaintiff's lawsuit, and order the plaintiff to bear the litigation costs. Lawsuits filed by the Municipal Council to recover house taxes are common, but Gan's defense is unprecedented and novel. The case was heard by Judge Xu Fuji of the First Special Court the day before yesterday. Both the plaintiff and the defendant were represented by lawyers. The plaintiff's lawyer stated the amount of tax owed by the defendant and presented the tax bill. The defendant's lawyer, Ge Zhaoji, then presented each of the above ten reasons one by one. The court then ordered both parties to withdraw and await the verdict. On the same day, Judge Xu summoned several others who were accused of owing house taxes, including the Paochouchang Tianfaxiang Fur Shop, etc. However, the purpose of these few companies in not paying house tax was not to demand the right to vote like Gan, but to litigate with conditions.

Jinglong Chemical Factory: Fire Extinguishing Bomb Demonstrated Yesterday, Fire Extinguished with One Bomb 157

The Jinglong Chemical Industry Factory, recently invented a kind of Jinglong vacuum natural fire extinguishing bomb by Wu Xiangyuan, the factory director. At about 4:00 PM yesterday, a wooden house was built on the open space of the Aodian Cinema on North Sichuan Road. The house and its surroundings were burned with flammable materials. When the fire was extremely fierce, the fire extinguishing bomb was thrown into the wooden house, and the fire was extinguished immediately. The factory invited representatives from various groups and manufacturers to watch the demonstration. Several hundred people witnessed the results and praised it. According to Wu Xiangyuan, the factory director, this fire extinguishing bomb is made of a liquid substance mixed with several kinds of secret chemical drugs, and is placed in a glass bomb using a vacuum method, so there is no danger of air leakage and the drug solution is effective forever. If this bomb is thrown into the midst of a raging fire and broken, its drug solution will turn into two kinds of non-flammable gases, absorbing a large amount of oxygen, and can immediately and universally extinguish the fierce fire.

Shengsheng Hospital: Establishes Regulations for Quitting Smoking, Reducing Pain, Safe Quitting, Especially Suitable for Women to Quit 160

Shengsheng Hospital was transformed from the Qu Family Hospital, a couple's hospital of Dr. Qu Shaohang and female doctor Yao Yingnai, who moved to Shanghai from Peiping. This time, the government strictly prohibits opium and drugs, and the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau has designated the hospital as a hospital for quitting smoking and verification. Therefore, it has drafted regulations for quitting smoking, which are specially recorded as follows: "(Article 1) This hospital is designated by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau as a hospital for quitting smoking and verification. Anyone who voluntarily wants to quit smoking and verification can come to the hospital for quitting and verification. (Article 2) This hospital selects the latest and best methods for quitting smoking, hoping that those who smoke due to illness and those who have been addicted to smoking for a long time can safely quit without pain. (Article 3) This hospital's fees for quitting smoking are divided into the following three types: (A) Inpatient quitting: 4 yuan per day for first-class rooms, 2 yuan per day for second-class rooms, and 8 jiao per day for third-class rooms (the cost of quitting smoking medicine for each class is charged according to item B below). 1 yuan per day for ordinary rooms (including the cost of quitting smoking medicine). (B) Outpatient quitting: 5 jiao is charged for those who smoke 1 qian per day, 1 yuan for those who smoke 2 qian per day, and 3 jiao is added for each qian more than 2 qian. (C) Guaranteed quitting: regardless of whether it is inpatient or outpatient, the fee is based on quitting. The fee is set as follows: 1. For inpatients: 150 yuan for first-class rooms, 80 yuan for second-class rooms, and 40 yuan for third-class rooms. 2. For outpatients: 40 yuan to 80 yuan (a discount is given to those who are poor). Those who quit smoking at this hospital will be charged according to the above regulations, and those who use medicine or injections due to other diseases will still be charged according to the regulations. (Article 4) Those who quit smoking at this hospital as inpatients must pay for ten days first, and then pay again when the period expires, and the balance will be refunded. Those who guarantee to quit must pay the full amount in advance, and those who stop quitting halfway will not be refunded, including relatives and friends. (Article 5) Those who quit smoking at this hospital will be issued a certificate by this hospital after quitting, without additional charges, and will fill out a written guarantee for the hospital to keep on file for investigation. (Article 6) Those who have not quit smoking at this hospital and want to ask this hospital to verify their quit smoking status must stay at this hospital for three days first, and the hospital will verify that they are indeed not addicted to smoking, fill out a written guarantee, and pay the inpatient fees and certificate fees before a certificate can be issued. The certificate fee is generally 10 yuan. Those who are poor and have no ability, and are specially approved by the president of the hospital, can be given a discount. Those who quit smoking at this hospital as outpatients and want to obtain a certificate must follow the verification procedures, but are exempt from the certificate fee. (Article 7) Those who quit smoking as inpatients must obey the regulations of this hospital, and must not go out privately without the permission of the president of this hospital, otherwise it will be regarded as stopping quitting halfway." It is also known that the hospital is located at 59 Route Say Zoong in the French Concession. The western-style building is spacious, the location is quiet in the middle of the city, and female doctors provide consultations for women who quit smoking, which is especially suitable.

Iron Hua's Japanese Photography Exhibition 162

Mr. He Tiexue, a young artist from Guangzhou, visited Japan with the "Japanese Culture Observation Group" of Lingnan University in Guangzhou during this summer vacation. He traveled extensively through the Japanese islands, including Osaka, a center of commerce and industry; Kyoto and Nara, famous for their historical sites and lush greenery; Tokyo, full of European and American elements; Kobe and Yokohama, important commercial centers; Yokosuka, a military center; and Mount Fuji, the Five Lakes, Nikko, Hakone, and other places renowned for their scenery. He captured Japanese culture, customs, construction, historical sites, and scenic spots in his lens, resulting in over 700 photographs. Announcement by the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau: Simple Life Insurance Regulations (Continued) 172

Contract Amendments Chapter Five: Amendment of Contracts Article 35: The policyholder may make the following amendments to the insurance contract, except when insurance premiums are waived according to the provisions of Article 27: (1) Convert a whole life insurance contract to a term life insurance contract, but the sum insured may not be increased. (2) Reduce the originally stipulated insurance premium. A handling fee of 20 cents silver must be paid for requests for the aforementioned amendments. Article 36: For insurance contracts for which premiums have been paid for two years or more, the policyholder may request that the contract be converted to a single-premium insurance contract, but the sum insured after the conversion may not be less than 50 yuan. Article 37: When a policyholder requests an amendment to the insurance contract according to the provisions of Article 35 and Article 36, he/she shall complete an application form in the prescribed format, together with the insurance policy and insurance premium receipt, and submit them to the Insurance Bureau. The handling fee payable shall be paid by affixing postage stamps to the application form. When the Insurance Bureau approves the aforementioned request, it shall correct the insurance policy and insurance premium receipt and return them to the policyholder. Article 38: When the policyholder or beneficiary changes the representative specified in Article 10, he/she shall complete an application form in the prescribed format, together with the insurance policy and insurance premium receipt, and submit them to the original Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for correction and return. Article 39: When the policyholder, insured, or beneficiary requests a change of name, or the policyholder requests a change of beneficiary, he/she shall complete an application form for correcting the insurance policy, together with the insurance policy and insurance premium receipt, and submit them to the original Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for correction and return. Changing the original name or changing the beneficiary shall require the consent of the insured, and his/her signature and seal shall be affixed to the application form. Article 40: When the policyholder changes his/her address or the location for paying insurance premiums, he/she shall notify the original Insurance Bureau of his/her new address or the designated payment location. When the insured moves to another city, the policyholder shall notify the original Insurance Bureau of his/her new address, and the Bureau shall designate an Insurance Bureau nearest to the new address as his/her reporting bureau. Upon arrival at the new address, the insured shall report and register with the reporting bureau. Article 41: When the policyholder or beneficiary dies and his/her heir accepts the inheritance of the insurance contract, he/she shall complete an application form for correcting the insurance policy in the prescribed format, together with the insurance policy and insurance premium receipt, and submit them to the original Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for correction and return. The aforementioned request shall require the consent of the insured, and his/her signature and seal shall be affixed to the application form. Article 42: When the enjoyment of the beneficiary's right to benefit has been definitively established, he/she may freely transfer the right to others, but only to the following groups, legal entities, or individuals: (1) Non-profit public groups, legal entities, ancestral temples, or schools. (2) Relatives. Article 43: When transferring in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article, the beneficiary shall complete an application form for correcting the insurance policy in the prescribed format, with the transferor and transferee jointly signing and affixing their seals. If the insured is alive, he/she shall also sign and affix his/her seal. The application form shall be submitted to the original Insurance Bureau, together with the insurance policy and the following supporting documents, for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for correction and return: (1) If the transferee is a group or legal entity, a certificate proving that it is organized on a non-profit basis shall be submitted. (2) If the transferee is a relative, a certificate proving the relationship between the transferor and the transferee shall be submitted.

Contract Validity Chapter Six: Termination, Reinstatement, and Rescission of Insurance Contract Validity Article 44: When a policyholder requests to terminate the insurance contract midway, he/she shall complete an application form for terminating the contract in the prescribed format, together with the insurance policy and insurance premium receipt, and submit them to the original Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for processing. Article 45: When refunding the accumulated fund in accordance with the provisions of Article 42 of the Simple Life Insurance Law, the accumulated amount due shall be equal to the accumulated fund that should be under the insurance contract, multiplied by the following percentage: 80 percent for contracts that have been in effect for less than three years; 81 percent for contracts that have been in effect for less than four years; 82 percent for contracts that have been in effect for less than five years; and so on, increasing by one percent per year, but with a maximum limit of 98 percent. Article 46: When requesting a refund of the accumulated fund due to midway termination or lapse of the contract, the beneficiary shall complete an application form in the prescribed format, together with the insurance policy and insurance premium receipt, and submit them to the Insurance Bureau. Once the aforementioned request is approved, the Insurance Bureau shall issue a payment order for the amount to be refunded and deliver it to the beneficiary. The beneficiary shall sign and affix his/her seal on the payment order and collect the payment from the designated Insurance Bureau. The provisions of Article 31 shall apply mutatis mutandis to this article. Article 47: When the insurer suspends the validity of the insurance contract in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 1 of Article 19 of the Simple Life Insurance Law, it shall complete a notice and notify the policyholder. Article 48: Once the validity of the insurance contract is suspended, a payment order shall be completed for the accumulated fund to be refunded and delivered to the policyholder, who shall sign and affix his/her seal and collect the payment from the designated Insurance Bureau. Article 49: When the policyholder requests to reinstate the validity of the insurance contract, he/she shall complete an application form in the prescribed format, together with the insurance policy, insurance receipt, and the insurance premiums not paid during the lapse period, late fees, etc., and submit them to the original Insurance Bureau or the insurance collector dispatched by the Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for processing. When the policyholder requests to reinstate the validity of the insurance contract and also requests a premium loan in accordance with the law, he/she shall attach a statement to the aforementioned application form and complete an application form for a premium loan and submit it to the Insurance Bureau together. The provisions of Articles 12 to 14 shall apply mutatis mutandis to this article. Article 50: When the insurer rescinds the insurance contract in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 1 of Article 25 of the Simple Life Insurance Law, the procedures shall apply mutatis mutandis to the provisions of Article 47 and Article 48.

Premium Loan Chapter Seven: Insurance Premium Loan Article 51: The policyholder may request a loan in accordance with the provisions of Article 30 of the Simple Life Insurance Law. Article 52: Loans are divided into two types: (1) Loans for paying insurance premiums (hereinafter referred to as premium loans). (2) Cash loans. Article 53: The maximum amount of each premium loan shall not exceed the insurance premium for one year and the amount to be refunded at that time. If the repayment is in installments, the amount of each installment shall be at least equal to the amount of one month's insurance premium. Cash loans may be borrowed once a year, with a minimum amount of 10 yuan and a maximum amount not exceeding 50% of the amount to be refunded at that time. If the repayment is in installments, the amount of each installment shall not be less than 1 yuan. Article 54: The loan period shall be set at one year, and the loan may be continued upon expiration. Article 55: Before the loan period expires, if the insurance contract lapses or matures midway, or if the beneficiary or policyholder is able to receive the sum insured or the amount to be refunded due to other events, the loan period shall also terminate at the same time. Article 56: Interest on premium loans shall be calculated from the date of payment, and interest on cash loans shall be calculated from the date of the loan. The aforementioned interest shall be paid in full at the time of repayment or request for continued loan. If the policyholder repays before the loan period expires, the interest shall be calculated only up to the date of repayment. Article 57: The loan interest rate shall be determined and announced by the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau from time to time. Article 58: When a policyholder requests a loan, he/she shall complete an application form in the prescribed format and submit it to the original Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for approval. If the beneficiary is a third party, the aforementioned request shall require the consent of the third party, and his/her signature and seal shall be affixed to the application form together. Once the loan is approved, the following procedures shall be followed: (1) For premium loans, the Insurance Bureau shall complete and issue a loan notification to the policyholder. (2) For cash loans, the Insurance Bureau shall complete and issue a loan collection order to the policyholder. Article 59: When the policyholder receives the loan notification, he/she shall sign and affix his/her seal on the notification and submit it to the Insurance Bureau together with the insurance premium receipt for registration and return. When the policyholder receives the loan collection order, he/she shall sign and affix his/her seal on the order and collect the loan from the bureau or office specified in the order. When collecting the loan, the Insurance Bureau shall properly keep the loan collection order as a loan receipt, and return the order to the borrower upon repayment. Article 60: When the policyholder repays the loan, he/she shall submit the principal and interest due, together with the insurance policy, to the Insurance Bureau. The Insurance Bureau shall record the amount received on the insurance policy. Article 61: If the policyholder fails to repay the loan within one month after the due date, he/she shall be subject to a late fee in addition to interest. Article 62: When the policyholder requests to continue the loan upon expiration, he/she shall complete an application form in the prescribed format and submit it to the Insurance Bureau together with the interest due and the insurance policy. If the beneficiary is a third party, this request shall require the consent of the third party, and his/her signature and seal shall be affixed to the application form together. Article 63: If the policyholder fails to repay the loan upon expiration and the contract has lapsed due to exceeding the grace period, the loan owed shall be deducted from the accumulated fund stipulated in Article 24 of the Simple Life Insurance Law, calculated up to the date of expiration of the grace period.

Group Contracts Chapter Eight: Group Contracts Article 64: Employees of various government agencies, companies, banks, factories, schools, and other groups, if 15 or more people simultaneously enter into insurance contracts, may be handled in accordance with group contracts. Article 65: The insurance premiums for all policyholders in a group contract shall be collected and paid by the representative in full. Article 66: Insurance premiums for group contracts may be collected at a 5% discount. Article 67: A group contract may mutually elect one person as a representative, who shall complete a group contract application form in the prescribed format, together with individual application forms and the first insurance premium payable, and submit them to the Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for processing. However, the method and location for paying insurance premiums, which should be filled in on the individual application forms, may be omitted. The group contract application form shall truthfully fill in the following items and be signed and sealed by the representative: (1) Group name and address. (2) Representative's name and address. (3) Number of application forms. Article 68: After a group contract is concluded, if new contracts are added, the representative shall complete an application form for joining group insurance in the prescribed format, together with the application forms, and submit them to the Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for processing. If the newly joined contract is an existing insurance contract, the insurance premium receipt for that contract must be attached. Article 69: If a policyholder wishes to withdraw his/her insurance contract from a group contract, the representative shall complete an application form for withdrawing from group insurance in the prescribed format and submit it to the Insurance Bureau for forwarding to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for processing. If there is a change in the payment method and location after withdrawal, it shall also be clearly stated. After the Insurance Bureau approves the aforementioned request, a new insurance premium receipt shall be issued and delivered to the withdrawing policyholder. If the withdrawal of a policyholder from a group contract results in fewer than 15 people, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau shall reject the withdrawal or cancel the 5% discount for the group contract. Chapter Nine: Supplementary Provisions Article 70: The formats of various application forms shall be formulated by the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau and provided free of charge. Article 71: These regulations shall take effect on the same date as the Simple Life Insurance Law.

A Visit to the Kaicheng Sulfuric Acid Plant 173

— Jin Huating

From here, one can understand the importance of sulfuric acid in industry.

(1) The Relationship Between Sulfuric Acid and Industry

Sulfuric acid is a chemical with a wide range of uses in industry. Therefore, sulfuric acid can be called the foundation of all industries. If one wants to know whether a country's industry is developed, one can tell by the amount of sulfuric acid it needs each year. In the past, our country did not pay much attention to chemistry, and the self-manufacture of sulfuric acid was even more impossible. In recent years, however, the people of our country have gradually realized the importance of sulfuric acid in industry and military affairs, and have devoted themselves to research and careful imitation. However, it is still only in the armories of various places that small-scale sulfuric acid plants are attached to manufacture sulfuric acid for their own military applications. For other industries, due to the lack of large-scale sulfuric acid plants in the country producing large quantities of sulfuric acid, they still have to purchase foreign goods. According to a survey in the 21st year [of the Republic], the quantity of foreign sulfuric acid imported into various ports in the country is as follows: Kowloon 18,361 dan, Shanghai 12,203 dan, Tianjin 7,161 dan, Jiaozhou 7,109 dan, Dalian 2,345 dan, other ports 2,345 dan. Moreover, the market price of foreign sulfuric acid is not fixed, and is entirely controlled by foreigners. Taking Shanghai as an example, the highest price has reached more than 17 taels per case. Various acid-using factories often suffer from the heavy cost of raw materials, so that their products cannot compete with foreign goods. Therefore, in the past three to five years, the people of our country have become more aware that if the basic raw materials are controlled by others, it will be difficult for domestic industry to develop. Therefore, sulfuric acid plants have been established in various parts of the country in order to achieve the goal of self-manufacture and self-sufficiency. As of now, there are eight sulfuric acid plants established in the country (completely capitalized by Chinese). Although they cannot compete with the countries of the East and West, they have made much more progress than before.

(2) The Grand Scale of the Kaicheng Acid Plant

The colleagues of Kaicheng Sulfuric Acid Company also realized that sulfuric acid is of great importance to military affairs, and that there are no large-scale sulfuric acid plants in the country, so the sulfuric acid used by various industries has to be imported from abroad, and the outflow of cash every year is alarming. In order to develop domestic industry and to recover overflowing rights, they raised a huge sum of 872,000 yuan and organized and established Kaicheng Sulfuric Acid Company in September of the 20th year of the Republic [1931], and began preparing to build a factory. In January of the 21st year [1932], construction began on the bank of the Huangpu River on Yinhang Military Road. Unexpectedly, not long after the start of construction, the January 28th Incident broke out, and construction had to be suspended for five months. It was not until the end of June of the same year that construction could continue. At the end of January of the following year, the factory was completed. The factory authorities specifically set the start of manufacturing on January 28th, which is full of the meaning of self-alertness and not forgetting. The foundation of the factory covers an area of ​​more than 46.5 mu. The entire factory has a total of 30 ore burning furnaces (only 18 are currently open). It is large in scale and fully equipped, and is the largest sulfuric acid plant in the country. When the factory was founded, it first manufactured sulfuric acid, and then gradually expanded to manufacture inorganic and organic acids such as nitric acid, salt, and acetic acid. After several years of hard work, the entire sulfuric acid plant was completed. The iron factory produces three types of products: 66-degree concentrated acid, 58-degree tower acid, and 48-degree bao acid. Since its release, it has been tested by various factories in the country and is considered satisfactory. At the same time, foreign goods can no longer control the market. The market price, which used to be 17 taels per case, has now fallen to less than 10 taels. Looking at this, we are not worried about the influx of foreign goods, but only hope that domestic products can be developed. However, the main raw material for making acid is iron sulfide ore. Although there are several places in the country that produce it, the results of the trial use are not satisfactory. Therefore, the iron sulfide ore currently used by the factory, except for a part from Shuikoushan, Hunan, is purchased from Spain. The market price of Spanish ore is 32 yuan per ton, and the market price of Shuikoushan ore is 28 yuan per ton. The factory's lead chamber produces about 16 tons per day, using about 7 tons of ore per day, and an average of about 13 tons of lead per month. Nitric acid was originally made from Chilean nitrate, but from next month, it will be replaced by nitric acid from the local Tianli Light Gas Factory. The sales market covers the whole country, and the business is quite extensive.

(3) The Manufacturing Method and Uses of Sulfuric Acid

A. Manufacturing Method of Sulfuric Acid. There are two methods for manufacturing sulfuric acid: (1) Lead Chamber Process, (Chamber Process) (2) Contact Process, (Contael Process). Because the domestic market needs more dilute sulfuric acid (i.e. light sulfuric acid), the factory uses the lead chamber method. The manufacturing process is briefly described as follows: First, iron sulfide ore is manually hammered into small pieces of about one inch, and then placed in an ore burning furnace for burning. The ignition of the ore burning furnace only requires the use of coking coal once at the beginning of construction to heat the ore burning furnace. After that, the heat generated by the chemical reaction when the ore is burned is enough to maintain the heat of the ore burning furnace, and no more coal is needed. Put the ore into the heated furnace, and because it contains a lot of sulfur, it will burn and combine with the gas in the air to become sulfur dioxide gas, which is the first step of the project. This hot gas and air are introduced into the niter furnace through the flue, and the sulfuric acid and niter in the pot in the furnace are distilled to generate nitric acid gas, which is the second step of the project. The mixed gas of the seven descriptions still contains dust, so it must be passed into a dust removal chamber to remove it, which is the third step of the project. After the dust is removed by the dust removal chamber, it is introduced into the first Gay-Lussac tower through the flue. At the same time, a fine mist of nitric dilute acid is sprayed down from the top of the tower to convert a part of the sulfur dioxide and nitric acid into sulfuric acid and nitrous acid gas, which is the fourth step of the project. The sulfuric acid converted in the tower is discharged from the acid discharge pipe at the bottom of the tower, which is called tower acid. Its specific gravity is about 58 degrees on the Baume scale. This tower acid is the 58-degree dilute sulfuric acid sold by the company on the market. The sulfur dioxide and nitrous acid gas that have not been converted into sulfuric acid in the tower are successively introduced into the first, second, and third lead chambers, and fine mist of clean water is sprayed down from the top of each chamber to convert them all into dilute sulfuric acid, which is the fifth step of the project. The dilute sulfuric acid generated in the lead chamber is called chamber acid. Its specific gravity: the acid in the first lead chamber is about 52 degrees on the Baume scale, the acid in the second lead chamber is about 49 degrees, and the acid in the third lead chamber is mixed and mixed. The remaining gas passing through the lead chamber is then sequentially passed into the second and third lead towers through the ventilation pipe, and a fine mist of dilute sulfuric acid is sprayed down from the top of the tower to absorb the nitrous acid in the remaining gas. The resulting nitric dilute sulfuric acid is placed in an acid storage tank from the acid discharge pipe at the bottom of the tower, and is pumped back to the top of the first lead tower by acid-resistant Fengpu, and sprayed into the first lead tower, so that the nitrous acid gas it absorbs can then enter the lead chamber from the lead tower. If the exchange function of the three lead towers is like this, the nitrous acid gas can always circulate in the three lead chambers, and only a small part of the loss is supplemented by the nitric acid gas generated by the niter furnace. That is, the sulfuric acid sold by the company on the market includes three types: 48-degree dilute sulfuric acid, 58-degree dilute sulfuric acid, and 66-degree concentrated sulfuric acid. The so-called concentrated sulfuric acid is made by heating the chamber acid or tower acid to make it concentrated. It is no different from dilute sulfuric acid, but the amount of water it contains is different.

B. Uses of Sulfuric Acid. Since sulfuric acid is divided into dilute and concentrated types, its uses are also different. The uses of sulfuric acid are very wide, and almost all kinds of industries need sulfuric acid. The main uses are described as follows:

(1) Uses of Dilute Sulfuric Acid. The largest use of dilute sulfuric acid is to manufacture superphosphate of lime and ammonium sulfate and other artificial fertilizers, accounting for almost eight-tenths of all uses. In addition, the main uses are to manufacture mirabilite (i.e., Glauber's salt), soda ash, caustic soda, sodium sulfide, bleaching powder, phosphorus, iodine, and bromine, and other chemical industrial raw materials and medicines, sulfurous acid, hydrochloric acid, nitric acid, hydrofluoric acid, boric acid, carbonic acid, chromic acid, oxalic acid, tartaric acid, citric acid, and acetic acid, and other inorganic and organic acids, potassium, barium, calcium, magnesium, lead, iron, zinc, copper, and mercury, and other raw materials for sulfate, and also in the refining of copper, lead, nickel, platinum, and silver, and other metal materials, the production of batteries, the refining of mineral oil, sugar production, and starch, the manufacture of organic pigments, the manufacture of parchment paper, the manufacture of soda water, enamel, dyeing, and gilding, and other industries, dilute acid is also the main raw material. It is also used as a precipitant, neutralizer, dispensing agent, and chemical analysis in various industries.

(2) Uses of Concentrated Sulfuric Acid. Although the uses of concentrated sulfuric acid are not as wide as those of dilute sulfuric acid, the quantity is also quite large, about half that of dilute sulfuric acid. The most important uses are to manufacture fatty acids, concentrated nitric acid, desulfurized acids, pigments, gunpowder, explosives, rayon, and celluloid, and other raw materials, as well as to manufacture kerosene, refined Bang La powder, and various mineral oils, refined gold and silver, separate copper and silver, and absorb moisture in the air. As for the raw materials for manufacturing sulfuric acid, there are three types: one, nitric acid; two, iron sulfide ore; and three, air.

In addition, the Spanish ore purchased by the factory contains about 3/1000 of arsenic. Therefore, the 48-degree dilute acid produced contains about 5/10000 of arsenous acid, which is not suitable for batteries, the manufacture of tartaric acid, citric acid, soda water, starch, and sugar, and other industries. Therefore, two sets of arsenic removal devices are specially set up to manufacture 48-degree arsenic-free dilute acid for the use of the above-mentioned factories.

(4) China's Acid Production and Other Countries

In recent years, China has established sulfuric acid plants in eight places, including Guangdong, Guangxi, Sichuan, Henan, Hanyang, Shanxi, Tianjin, and Shanghai. The largest daily output is 15 tons for Shanghai Kaicheng and Henan Shanxi, and the smallest is 5 tons per day for Tianjin Lizhong Company. The rest are around 10 tons. The total annual output is about 295,200 tons. Looking at the annual acid production of various countries in the world, Japan is 1 million tons, the United States is 4 million tons, Russia is 700,000 tons, and the United Kingdom, Germany, and France are all 1.3 million tons. According to the ratio of these quantities, it is no wonder that China's industry is so backward.

When the reporter visited the Kaicheng Sulfuric Acid Plant the other day, he was personally guided by Mr. Lin Dazhong and Mr. Fang Lvxhi to visit, and they explained the manufacturing method and uses of sulfuric acid in detail, for which I am very grateful. Mr. Lin graduated from the Gunpowder Department of the Faculty of Engineering of Tokyo Imperial University. After returning to China, he worked in the Hanyang Arsenal for seven years and the Shanghai Arsenal for four years. After the 21st year [of the Republic], he began to preside over the Kaicheng Sulfuric Acid Plant. Mr. Fang graduated from Fukuoka Institute of Technology in Japan and is now a technician at the factory.

Niu Hongquan Wins Yesterday's Longhua Round Trip Long Run With a Time of 1:08:17.4. Wang Zhenglin Second, He Baoshan Third 178

The third Longhua round trip long run competition organized by the Xiguang Cross-Country Team started at 8:20 am yesterday in front of the Minli Middle School on Zhonghua Road. A total of 148 people participated. The entire course is 12 miles long, about 20,000 meters. Niu Hongquan, a new general from Chizhi University, finished the entire course with a record of 1:08:17.5, and won the championship this year. Wang Zhenglin finished second with a slight difference, with a time of 1:08:23.4. He Baoshan ranked third. Prizes were awarded on the spot after the competition, and the situation was very enthusiastic. The details are recorded as follows:

A Glimpse of the Departure - There were originally 215 people who signed up to participate in this year's long run race, but yesterday morning, due to the cold weather, strong winds, and slippery roads, only 148 people actually arrived. After the roll call was completed at 8:20 am, the start was made in front of Minli Middle School. With an order from the starter Shen Yuguang, 296 flying legs moved together, which was very good-looking. The referee and staff vehicles led the way, and the contestants brought their own guides to take care of them along the way by bicycle, so the process was very easy. However, due to the cold weather, the number of people who dropped out halfway was very large.

Situation Along the Way - In this competition, it was generally expected that Wang Zhenglin and He Baoshan had the best chance of winning the championship. After the start, when the advance reached the Xiejiao Manufacturing Bureau Road, the skinny monkey took the lead and led the crowd. He Shishan followed closely behind, unwilling to let go for two steps, while Niu Hongquan was still in the crowd at this time and did nothing. Later, when they turned into Xietu Road Luban Road, Lao Niu suddenly jumped out and ranked at the forefront. Wang Zhenglin ranked second, and He Baoshan retreated to third, while Li Duan and Zhang Liang gradually fell behind, far apart. After passing the Jingbei Command Headquarters of Nanyang Middle School at Rihui Bridge and arriving at the bottom of Longhua Pagoda, the battle line remained unchanged. When they turned back to Xiaoximen Daxing Street, Wang Zhenglin and He Baoshan drove side by side, and the difference from Niu Hongquan was only one shoulder. The competition was extremely fierce at this time, but at the finish line, Lao Niu took the lead and won the championship. The skinny monkey relied on his final sprint to surpass He Baoshan by one shoulder and ranked second. He Shishan retreated to third. Li Duan, Han Youhai, etc. finished the entire course, a total of 40 people.

A reporter visited Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, yesterday to inquire about the recent state of education in the city. The Education Bureau has advanced over 100,000 yuan in various items for necessary temporary expenses. Therefore, regarding school funding, the August expenses for schools in the first district of the city have not yet been fully paid, and, in addition to borrowing a portion of the September expenses for schools in rural areas, a huge amount of school funding is owed. Both the Education Bureau and the schools feel extremely difficult. When I returned to Shanghai this time, I repeatedly consulted with Mayor Wu and Secretary-General Yu, who promised to find a way for the Finance Bureau to issue the payment notices for the September expenses first and instructed the Municipal Treasury to expedite the payments, in order to first pay off the outstanding amounts for August and September to the schools. Because I had to go to Beijing, I instructed the head of the relevant section to continue to liaise for the allocation of funds before I left. At a time when the city's finances are strained, this bureau is doing its best to find solutions, but it hopes that all agencies and schools can also share the difficulties and overcome the challenges together. Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (112) 198

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

I've been putting them in all the time, but it just won't fill up. I'm really tired, said Rob, stopping to rest his short legs, and beginning to think berry-picking was not as pleasant as he had imagined; for the sun was high, and still had some power to burn, and Nan was jumping about like a grasshopper, tipping the berries out of his pail as fast as he put them in; for she knew by experience that said pail was given to sudden fits of turning over.

“The berries were lots thicker on the other side of the wall last time we came,—and ever so much bigger; and there's a cave over there, where the boys made a fire once. Let's go over, and fill our pails real quick, and then hide in the cave, and let them come and find us,” proposed Nan, who was quite ready for a new adventure.

Rob agreed, and away they went, scrambled over the wall, and ran down the sloping field on the other side, till they were deep among the rocks and bushes. Here the berries were so thick that the pails were soon full; and there the ground was shady and cool, and a little spring trickled from its mossy cover to give the thirsty children a sweet draught.

Nan felt that getting over the wall was quite an achievement, and could not resist saying, “Now let's go and rest in the cave, and eat our luncheon.”

“Do you know the way?” asked Rob.

“Of course I do; I came once, and I never forget. Didn't I go and fetch my trunk myself?”

Page 17

Economic Review

A Study on Implementing Equal Sales of Rice 199

— Li Yinbei

I. An Investigation of Grain Trade in the Interior

"Cheap grain harms farmers, expensive grain harms the people." This ancient saying remains a clear instruction today. Currently, grain prices sometimes surge and sometimes plummet, creating a very serious social problem. Although the fluctuations in grain prices are closely related to the issues of imported rice, natural disasters, and political problems in recent years, the failure to adjust the surplus and deficit of grain in various parts of the interior is also an important factor. For example, in the past few years, wheat was used as fuel in some areas, while in other rural areas, people were reduced to cannibalism due to famine. In fact, the overall food problem in China has never been addressed with adjustment methods. For example, if a certain place has always had insufficient grain, what is the amount of the shortage, and how should adjustment be initiated? If a certain place has a surplus of grain, what is the amount of the surplus, and what methods should be used to transport the grain to areas in need? Is the total grain production in the country sufficient to balance the consumption of the entire population? If the national grain production is insufficient for the consumption of the entire population, what methods should be used to adjust the shortage? Conversely, if there is a surplus of grain production, how can outlets be found for the grain, ensuring that cheap grain does not harm farmers when there is a surplus and that expensive grain does not harm the people when there is a shortage? However, to achieve this goal, it is impossible without implementing (equal sales) of grain throughout China. To implement equal sales of grain, it is necessary to start with the issue of grain surplus and deficit in the interior. To understand the surplus and deficit of grain in the interior, it is essential to begin with investigations. Only after investigation can the degree of grain surplus and deficit in the interior be expressed numerically. The Rural Reconstruction Commission, based on this objective, specifically entrusted the Shanghai Social and Economic Research Institute to conduct grain investigations in Shanghai, Nanjing, Jiangxi, Wuhu, Wuxi, and other places. However, in terms of methodology, it is always assumed that conditions are the same everywhere without having investigated in the interior. Furthermore, the degree of similarity is based on the methods used in the Shanghai investigation. In reality, this is incorrect. Methods applicable to area A are not necessarily applicable to area B; methods applicable to one time are not necessarily applicable to another. The food organization in Shanghai is different from that in Wuxi, and Nanjing cannot be considered the same either. Thus, those who hold great hope and personally enter the interior to investigate the grain surplus and deficit will be disappointed and give up because they did not pay attention to the time and space aspects of the methodology. This methodological issue restricts the entire grain investigation work. Therefore, we will describe what we have seen and understood below.

II. Methods of Collecting Data

We rely on the cooperation of transportation agencies as the most important source for investigating grain surplus and deficit. In summary, the following places are where data on grain surplus and deficit problems arise:

(1) Customs reports

(2) Railway freight records

(3) Highway freight records

(4) Account books of transfer businesses in various places

(5) Inland waterway shipping business account books

(6) Freight vouchers of boat transport businesses in various counties

Among the materials from the above six aspects, only customs reports and railway transportation records are currently available. Highway freight business is also not very important. As for the transportation materials of transfer businesses, inland waterway shipping businesses, and boat transport businesses in various counties, they have not been collected at all. In Shanghai, the investigation of grain trade mostly focuses on customs reports and railway freight records, multiplied by the total population of Shanghai to estimate the grain surplus and deficit. However, this investigation method is only applicable to Shanghai, a national grain distribution center, and is not suitable for the interior. The only method for investigating grain in the interior is to start with the grain trade situation and population survey in various places. Regarding the population issue, the household registration system in the interior can be used, and liaison can be made with administrative authorities. Even if the obtained materials are not entirely accurate and detailed, there should not be major discrepancies. The difficulty lies in how to start the investigation of grain trade in the interior.

We believe that the most important issue in the grain surplus and deficit in the interior is, of course, how much grain is imported into a certain place each year. The main sources of this data are the grain merchants and other institutions engaged in grain trade in the area. The concrete representation of the annual grain trade of these grain merchants and grain trading institutions is the account book. And the most important one is, of course, the "source of goods" account. Because the grain imported into the interior is traditionally divided into "local goods" and "foreign goods." "Local goods" reflect the surplus and deficit of local grain production; "foreign goods" reflect the surplus and deficit of grain transportation and sales in a certain place. All quantities of these two types of grain imported into a place are recorded in the source of goods account. And according to the study of material sources in statistics: the "source of goods" account can be listed as one of the "primary materials," whose accuracy is more reliable than any other data.

However, grain merchants often have a mysterious and elusive attitude. They are usually unwilling to easily show these types of account books. Firstly, due to business reasons, it is indeed necessary to strictly maintain confidentiality. Secondly, the issue of political taxes has undermined the trust of grain merchants, and there is also a considerable component of keeping account books secret. For example, the Social and Economic Research Institute encountered the unresolved issue of collecting wheat business tax during its investigation of grain in Wuxi. In this atmosphere of extreme suspicion, it became very difficult for investigators to collect estimates of the total annual grain imports, to the point where "knocking on the door ten times, nine times it remains unopened." It is simply a dream to collect the account books of grain merchants. I am afraid this lesson is deeply imprinted in the minds of the investigators. Although the investigation is an investigation and has nothing to do with the business tax issue, we know the psychology of the grain merchants; due to the lessons of past tax payments, they inevitably have some "bow and snake shadow" fears. The helplessness of grain merchants is an undeniable fact.

As for remedial measures, it is not to say that there are absolutely none; however, before the government's credibility can be established among the people, we believe that investigators must help themselves. The following four suggestions are the spiritual tools that investigators should have.

(A) Investigators must clarify the purpose of the investigation. Before starting the investigation, clarifying the purpose of the investigation is a necessary preliminary step. Often, many investigators neglect this initial step that should be clarified; even if they do clarify, it is vague and unclear. As a result, when grain merchants encounter investigators, they cannot understand their purpose and cannot dispel their suspicions. The cunning ones are perfunctory, while the resistant ones refuse to open their doors. In the end, they piece together unreliable materials from various sources to fulfill their responsibilities. Therefore, we cannot ignore the issue of clarifying the purpose. For example, if we are investigators directly under the administrative authority, we should explain the purpose of this investigation; if there are benefits for grain merchants, we must make grain merchants believe that these benefits are possible and not deceptive. If grain merchants have grievances to express, they should be sincerely accepted; it is best to trace the source of the grievances and find ways to alleviate them to comfort them.

(B) Focus on political power and use public opinion as a means of entry. Past investigators have overlooked this avenue of investigation. Observe a group of investigators going to a place; they either use an official letter to ask the local administrative authority for assistance, or they first submit a request to the competent authority of the administrative authority in a certain place, requesting them to issue an instruction to the administrative authority in a certain place to help. These methods all use administrative power as the main force, which is no longer suitable in modern society. Moreover, administrative power may not be applicable to our economic investigation work; perhaps a general report can be done, but obtaining precise and reliable statistics is probably something that administrative agencies cannot do. We believe that the best way is to start by contacting the public opinion agencies in the interior and ask them to be our investigation tools. Let us reason: public opinion is a loudspeaker that speaks for the people every day and talks closely with the people every day; compared to the function of an official letter or an instruction, it is much healthier in spirit. As long as public opinion agrees to help, any problem can be easily solved.

(C) Investigators must be socially educational and not politically bureaucratic. When investigators from any agency investigate this kind of economic grain issue, they should always take a social perspective and use educational means as a prerequisite. Because the nature of our investigation is to focus on research for consultation, not management or execution, based on the distinction in nature, we should only use means of food education and absolutely not contain any bureaucratic elements. Even in terms of the effectiveness of the investigation, the former is superior.

(D) Investigation questions should focus on outlines and abandon details. To be honest, most of the people who can preside over investigation work have undergone scientific thought training. Every question can be arranged into a web of questions in a deductive manner. Applying this web of questions to an equal level, it is not difficult to obtain satisfactory answers. However, the representatives of grain merchants in the interior are old-fashioned merchants, not new intellectuals. There are certainly some who have received scientific thought training, but on the whole, old-fashioned merchants are the majority. Therefore, if the investigation questions of the grain investigators are too complicated, they not only cannot answer them, but also find them annoying. Based on this test, when investigators discuss issues with representatives of grain merchants, they should focus on the main points of the concrete outline; it is best not to talk about unimportant issues.

The above four methods must be modified in application according to the social conditions of the interior. If you can follow these principles, you will surely succeed. In short, we all know that everyone has a responsibility and a vested interest in the total bankruptcy of the national rural areas; the purpose of investigating grain surplus and deficit is to revive the rural areas to prosper the cities. The reason why grain merchants in the interior are unwilling to report the trade situation truthfully to us is not that they do not support the joint revival of the rural areas; it is because they are afraid that after revealing everything, it will be detrimental to themselves. Among them, the most suspicious maze is the tax issue. At this point, investigators can only take a position of non-deception before political credibility is obtained with the trust of the people; they should focus on the above four principles to train themselves. We hope that our investigators will henceforth abide by this as a motto for investigation work.

III. The Importance of Average Rice Sales

Rice is a necessary consumer product for the livelihood of our people. In recent years, due to the intermingling of natural disasters and man-made calamities, the area suitable for rice cultivation has been shrinking daily. According to the estimate of the Statistics Bureau of the National Government's Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, the annual rice production in our country is 61,113,780,000 catties, which is only enough for 191,600,000 people to eat (see the Social and Economic Monthly Report, Volume 2, Issue 3, page 48). If this figure is reliable, then there are more than 200 million people whose food is not available. Needless to say, this is not really unavailable, but the rice obtained is not produced by China's own farmland. As for how profound this rice panic is, it can be glimpsed from the historical imported rice figures.

If we want to think about the rice problem, then we can only get rid of this restriction through the means of (1) expanding the area of arable land, (2) improving agricultural technology, and (3) implementing average sales. But on the first point; Mr. [blank] of [blank] in the United States estimates that China has little hope in this short period of time. The reason is that only 29% of China's total land is arable farmland; the remaining 70% of the land is either dry due to climate and lack of rain, or mountainous and barren; and many good fertile lands are often occupied by the tombs of feudal society, making good land unusable. From this inference, expanding the area of land can certainly increase rice production; but it may not be realized in the short term. On the second point, it is indeed an economical way to increase rice production, but because it is not the subject discussed in this article, it is the third point listed for the implementation of average [blank]. Before discussing this issue, we should first understand what average sales are. Simply put: average sales includes two meanings; one is that consumers implement "equal distribution," and the other is that producers implement "joint sales." In short, if this kind of average rice sales can really be implemented, at the very least, it can eliminate the concept of "self-interest and wealth" in trading behavior. Now we list a few of the average sales systems that have taken preliminary shape in our country for review.

(1) Sales cooperatives: Sales cooperatives are the cornerstone of "joint sales" under the average sales system; accounting for a section of the entire average sales business. Its business is to entrust the cooperative to sell the rice produced by the farmers. Although the purpose of the sales cooperative is to sell directly to consumers without going through the hands of rice middlemen; the potential power in the urban areas of the commercial society is heavily guarded; it is really "difficult to clap with one hand" to penetrate the city with the organization of a sales cooperative.

(2) Agricultural warehouses: Although warehouses are not executive agencies for implementing average sales; they are an important organization to assist average sales. In terms of rice consumers, it can help consumers "distribute evenly"; in terms of rice producers, it can help producers "sell jointly." However, the current warehouses are not directly operated by rice consumers or rice producers; most of the warehouses are either storage for rice or accounting rooms for banks.

(3) Rice sales control: Rice sales control is the policy of average rice sales. In other words, it is a kind of controlled economy; originally, the controlled economy is the latest economic policy, and many countries have adopted it. The purpose of rice sales control: the first step is to manage rice middlemen to order rice from abroad, so that the price of rice in the country will not be harmed by excessive imports of foreign rice. The second step is to count the domestic rice consumption and production, and use political power to adjust it; and according to the agricultural season, stipulate the price of rice; so that middlemen who operate rice business must not arbitrarily manipulate the market. The third step is to build extremely large warehouses in the important rice distribution centers in the country to store the surplus rice in the area; to regulate the food supply in areas lacking rice. If this method can be effectively implemented, the purpose of average rice sales may be achieved. However, this kind of sales control has not yet been realized in our country; last year, the eight-province grain marketing bureau that the central government wanted to organize but failed was a kind of average rice sales control method.

IV. Conclusion

In conclusion: the meaning of average rice sales is nothing more than the concrete manifestation of making the production economy and the consumer economy work together effectively. In the three methods described above: we find that there are four conditions for average sales:

The first is the storage conditions of rice; checking the rice itself is originally a troublesome thing to manage; after the implementation of average rice sales, the separate storage of farmers will be changed to centralized storage. The storage equipment of centralized storage and separate storage is very different. In terms of storage problems, ventilation equipment, moisture-proof equipment, insect-proof equipment, and rat-proof equipment all require attention; otherwise, a slight negligence will harm the entire sales system, which is no small matter! The second is the conditions for rice processing and preparation: all milling must be given considerable attention. The third is the rice marketing conditions; the fourth is the rice financial conditions.

Under the organization of sales cooperatives, due to the poverty of the cooperatives, the storage and processing of rice are always perfunctory. The marketing conditions also cannot be achieved in every detail; and even the financial conditions are difficult to truly achieve the principles of agricultural finance. Secondly, under the organization of the warehouse system, although it can barely be done in storage and processing; it is still far from the perfect warehouse principles. According to the records of the Rural Reconstruction Committee, among the warehouses established in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces, only the Dongting warehouse in Wuxi, Jiangsu, meets the warehouse principles; most of the remaining warehouses are rented houses, ancestral halls, and temples in order to save expenses at the time of opening. As for this kind of leased building, it has already been in disrepair for many years; the safety of rice is mostly dangerous! As for the marketing conditions, although they have not been achieved: but in fact, they have no way to achieve it. Even in terms of financial conditions: there is not a single warehouse that does not take the attitude of "storage is mortgage"; therefore, storage and mortgage are not separated, where can rice talk about average sales? What is the rice sales control; because we have not seen the grain marketing bureau open for business; so it is impossible to predict it here.

Finally, we believe that this kind of unsystematic average sales; the method is wrong. If this continues, not only will it not reach the purpose of average sales; but it will also disrupt the order of the food organization. The future remedy is only to cooperate from both the "official" and the "people" aspects. On the government side, the Rice Average Sales Committee or the National Grain Marketing Bureau must be established immediately to control the import of foreign rice, count the rice surplus and deficit in each province, manage the national agricultural warehouses, and register the mills, rice mills, privately operated rice mills, and other processing matters related to rice; all matters related to winemaking and sugar making must also be included in the restrictions. On the people's side; they must earnestly inherit the government's control policy of average sales, organize sales cooperatives and consumer cooperatives, cooperate from top to bottom, so that the purpose of average sales can truly be achieved.

A Discussion on Promoting Rural Side Occupations 200

— Ji Jun

In recent years, rural side occupations have been widely valued by the general public, and efforts have been made to promote them. However, promoting rural side occupations seems very simple on the surface, but it is not simple in reality.

The prerequisite for promoting side occupations is to recognize the basic principles, and then talk about the methods and steps of promotion. Now, please explain in detail.

A. Basic Principles for Promoting Side Occupations

(1) Adapting to the environment: The standard for promoting side occupations should be determined according to the environment and products of each place. For example, in places where mats are produced, the mat-making industry should be promoted; in places where mulberry is produced, attention should be paid to silkworm breeding, silk weaving, and silk floss making. The age and physical strength can also affect the type of side occupations promoted.

(2) Not hindering the main occupation: The promotion of side occupations should be based on the principle of not hindering the main occupation.

(3) Reducing costs and making the business easy: Low costs make it possible for farmers to afford them, and it is easier to sell. The business is easy, does not require many tools, and does not occupy much area, so that men, women, and young girls in rural areas can work anytime and anywhere. If the business occupies a large area or requires a lot of funds, it may be difficult to promote it widely.

(4) Utilizing raw materials: Maximize the use of the original raw materials in various places, preferably the by-products of the main occupation. For example, in areas where wheat is produced, promote the production of [blank] whips; in this way, the raw materials can be widespread, and there is no need to spend more costs, then the side occupations will naturally move towards development. Otherwise, even if there is a good plan, but the local area lacks raw materials and purchases from other places, the cost will be large, the profit will be small, and the promotion of side occupations will be difficult. It is also a pity to discard the local raw materials!

(5) Finding ways to expand sales channels: Sometimes, even if there are excellent products, but because there are few consumers, or they have not been promoted to distant places, it is difficult to sell, which affects the business's lack of progress. Therefore, after having a large number of products, in addition to supplying local consumption, they should be sold to the outside world; when the products sell well and have a commercial position, then that side occupation will naturally develop.

(6) Excellent products: To have excellent products, first select good raw materials, return to the original manufacturing, and improve manufacturing methods. For example, in the cotton areas of Tongchonghai and Qiru counties in Jiangsu, weaving cloth has always been a side occupation, and a lot of coarse cloth is produced; but now, because the market and consumers have different needs, coarse cloth is blocked. When we promote side occupations here, we should make them change to using fine yarn to weave cloth that sells well in the market, in order to sell well.

(7) Improving transportation and sales: Most of the products of farmers' side occupations are still controlled by merchants, and they cannot be sold at a good price, which greatly affects the business. It is best to organize transportation and sales cooperatives, where producers sell directly without going through middlemen. At the same time, improve the methods of loading, transportation, and storage, so that they can be transported to distant places without loss, especially for fruits and eggs.

B. Procedures for Implementing Promotion

The procedure for promoting side occupations should first be investigated, and the results of the investigation should be used to divide the areas of side occupations; and also emphasize the situation of various side occupations in the market as a reference for promoting the business. Secondly, organize the original side occupations, because the original business has a long history, and rural residents have some experience and training in skills and situations. We only need to organize or improve them, and they will naturally develop; after having a foundation in this aspect, we will then select one or two of the most suitable side occupations to promote. That being said, if the original side occupations are really not enough to maintain, we do not have to introduce new businesses unchanged to replace the original side occupations. In short: we must pay attention to reality, and we must not ignore reality.

The above is only a rough outline. The detailed methods vary according to the business - such as side occupations in the industrial sector, which are a method of promotion; and side occupations in the agricultural sector, which are another method of promotion - and vary from place to place. It is up to those who are responsible for promoting rural side occupations to determine them in a timely and event-based manner. This article will not repeat them!
