Special Issue on Lung Disease

Advice to Coughing Patients 210

— Physician Shen Zhaoquan

Coughing is an opposing movement of the airways. It often begins with a deep breath, followed by an opposing movement of the airways. A sudden, forceful expulsion of phlegm occurs, opening the closed glottis. The sound produced at this time is called a cough. Healthy individuals generally cough due to inhaling strong air, catching a cold, or irritation of the trachea and throat by smoke and dust. However, irritation of the ear canal or root of the tongue can also trigger a cough. Coughs are often caused by asthma, bronchitis, laryngitis, tuberculosis, emphysema, whooping cough, pharyngitis, airway ulcers, and small tumors in the larynx, as well as various other respiratory diseases. When a person coughs, the systemic venous circulation is disrupted, causing the veins in the forehead and neck to swell, with distinct blue veins becoming visible. The face may turn pale and red. This phenomenon is readily observable. Furthermore, increased pressure in the lungs can lead to emphysema.

Common coughs invariably involve the expectoration of phlegm. Coughs without phlegm are called dry coughs, which can be caused by irritation of the ear canal, laryngitis, bronchitis, or whooping cough. Healthy individuals only cough when smoke, dust, or other irritants enter the airways. Those with respiratory illnesses may cough immediately after inhaling cold air or air containing dust. However, there are exceptions. If the patient is unconscious, the throat or bronchi are already paralyzed, or the respiratory muscles are weakened due to chronic bronchitis (such as in children with underdeveloped muscles or individuals with weakened respiratory muscles due to fever), coughing may be difficult even when there is a cause for it.

Phlegm can have several characteristics, but generally consists of mucus, pus, and epithelial cells. Sometimes it contains blood cells, strong fibers, or tuberculosis bacteria, which are only present in certain diseases.

Even minor coughs should be treated immediately. Ignoring them can easily lead to serious conditions such as pneumonia and tuberculosis. As the saying goes, "A cold that doesn't heal turns into consumption." Therefore, prompt treatment is essential.

Anyone who has had a cough due to a cold for more than three weeks should suspect tuberculosis and seek medical attention early. Do not let it go untreated.

The treatment for coughing depends on the cause but generally aims to resolve phlegm and suppress the cough. Commonly used medications include Tr. Ipeacacuanha, Tr. Senega, Ammonia Chlorate, Tolu Balsam, and Codeine. Therefore, cough drops and cough syrups sold on the market are generally made from these ingredients. They have limited effectiveness and can easily harm the appetite, making them unsuitable for long-term use.

Recently, I have been using "Fei Huo" (Lung Reviver), Phith Weal, to treat coughs, asthma, and shortness of breath with rapid and effective results. It is superior to all other cough medications. The medicine is sweet and palatable, making it easy for women and children to take. Long-term use does not harm the appetite. This medication can effectively relieve coughing from old age, phlegm, tuberculosis, colds, and other coughs on the same day and cure them within days. Furthermore, taking "Fei Huo" helps improve health and prevent tuberculosis. It is especially recommended for those with weak constitutions, weak lungs, and excessive phlegm.

The Foundation of Tuberculosis Recovery 211

— Physician Jiang Guanqun

The quality of nutrition is closely related to the progression of tuberculosis in patients. Poor nutrition leads to weakness, weight loss, and accelerated disease progression. Conversely, good nutrition leads to weight gain and gradual improvement in the disease. The patient's weight and body build are often used to determine the stage of tuberculosis. Therefore, good nutrition and weight gain are the foundation of tuberculosis recovery.

To achieve good nutrition, it is important to eat nutritious and easily digestible foods, such as animal products like meat, fish, milk, and eggs, as well as plant products like rice, wheat, beans, and vegetables. It is important not to favor one type over the other and to consume both animal and plant-based foods. It is also important to eat a variety of foods instead of relying on a single item. The body requires various nutrients (i.e., protein, fat, carbohydrates, vitamins, etc.) in proper proportions for nourishment. No single food contains all of these nutrients. Therefore, eating only one type of food every day can lead to an excess or deficiency of certain nutrients, making it difficult to achieve a balanced diet. Furthermore, even the best foods can become unappealing if eaten every day for a long time, leading to a loss of appetite. Therefore, tuberculosis patients should eat a variety of foods.

A healthy digestive system is the foundation of tuberculosis treatment. To achieve good nutrition, the digestive system must be healthy. A healthy digestive system directly affects appetite. Food should be chewed thoroughly to allow saliva to mix with it before swallowing. If food is swallowed too quickly without proper chewing, digestion will be incomplete, and the amount of nutrients absorbed by the body will be reduced, diminishing its nutritional value. This can lead to fatigue in the digestive system, causing indigestion and malnutrition. The key to curing tuberculosis lies in strengthening the body to overcome the tuberculosis bacteria. However, the absorption ability of tuberculosis patients is often weak, leading to poor nutrition. Therefore, consuming large amounts of food may not be digestible or absorbable, and may even worsen gastrointestinal problems.

Of the nutrients required by the human body, protein is the most important, followed by carbohydrates and fats. Other inorganic salts and vitamins are needed in much smaller amounts. With the exception of protein, the other nutrients can be sufficiently absorbed from ordinary foods. However, protein requires the most effort and complex digestion to obtain. Therefore, it is difficult for tuberculosis patients, who have weak digestive systems, to obtain sufficient protein from their daily diet.

Therefore, tuberculosis patients must seek protein supplements in addition to ordinary foods. However, many of the tonics sold on the market often contain only small amounts of phosphorus, arsenic, iron, calcium, iodine, etc., and offer little actual benefit, sometimes even harming the digestive system and hindering recovery. Tuberculosis patients should be very careful when purchasing tonics.

"Kang's Life Element" (Conbour's Sanvita-Cell) is made from animal protein that has been completely digested artificially using enzymes. It contains various essential amino acids. It can be absorbed directly by the body without digestion, nourishing the body, producing blood, and building muscle. It also encourages cells to promote metabolism and rejuvenate the whole body, increasing the secretion of digestive juices to aid digestion. It also plays a key role in disease resistance, brain development, physical activity, and reproductive organ function. The toxins produced by tuberculosis cause severe protein breakdown in the body, making it appropriate to take this product to supplement protein deficiency. Furthermore, this product enhances nutrition in tuberculosis patients, naturally increasing their healing power and resistance. Therefore, it is an important medicine for treating tuberculosis. Taking this medicine can achieve twice the result with half the effort.

In my years of treating tuberculosis, I have consistently prescribed "Kang's Life Element" (Conbour's San-Vita-Cell) and "Fei Huo" (Phith Weal) for patients to take internally, along with instructions to rest, seek fresh air and sunlight, and pay close attention to their diet and living conditions. Lecture on Neurasthenia 212

The Destroyer of Family Happiness: Dysfunction of the Reproductive Organs

— (Physician Shen Xiangbo)

Causes and Treatment of Impotence

Impotence, commonly known as kidney deficiency, is a very broad symptom. It essentially involves the complete loss of the ability to perform sexual intercourse, resulting in infertility. It deprives couples of the joys of intimacy, leading to discord and increased distress. Therefore, impotence can be said to be a destroyer of family happiness.

There are many causes of impotence, broadly classified into three categories: diseases and abnormalities of the reproductive organs, lack of excitability in the erection center, and psychological disorders related to reflexes. These are described below:

(1) Impotence caused by diseases and abnormalities of the reproductive organs: This category includes dozens of symptoms. The most severe is organic impotence, caused by deformities, phimosis, defects, or underdevelopment of the reproductive organs, or by abnormalities near the penis. However, even in these cases, depending on the severity of the symptoms, reproductive function may not be completely lost.

(2) Impotence caused by lack of excitability in the erection center: This is caused by damage to the erection nerves, often accompanied by decreased or complete loss of libido. This is due to chronic gonorrhea and syphilis, tuberculosis, kidney disease, myelitis, obesity, and other diseases affecting the prostate or urethral glands. Sexual excitement is completely obstructed, resulting in impotence due to the loss of stimulation to the libido center. Intoxication from alcohol, tobacco, opium, morphine, arsenic, etc., can also be a cause. In particular, excessive masturbation and sexual intercourse can lead to loss of excitability in the erection and ejaculation centers, a condition known as masturbatory impotence.

(3) Impotence caused by psychological disorders related to reflexes: This is caused by strong mental emotions such as fright, worry, shame, anger, and terror. Some pure young men fear contracting syphilis and are plagued by obsessive thoughts, leading to impotence. Furthermore, inventors who are engrossed in scientific pursuits may concentrate their minds on a particular area, resulting in impotence. The causes of impotence are indeed varied and numerous.

Treatment for impotence: Because impotence is not an independent disease but rather caused by various factors, the underlying cause must be treated first. Generally speaking, impotence is often reversible. Based on my clinical experience, the most effective medication for treating impotence is the endocrine preparation "Huan Er Tong" (Well Tonic). Simply follow the directions for use (two tablets three times a day before meals), and it is almost certain to be effective. However, strict adherence to health rules is also necessary during the treatment period. Avoid excessive consumption of stimulating foods and drinks (such as tobacco, alcohol, coffee, spicy peppers, onions, garlic, etc.). Favor nutritious foods such as milk, eggs, meat broth, chicken broth, and fish. If impotence is caused by physical weakness or anemia, "Huan Er Tong" (Well Tonic) should be combined with a blood-tonifying agent. "Kang's Life Element" (Conbour's San-Vita-Cell) is the best blood-tonifying medicine. Other important measures include avoiding physical and mental overexertion and engaging in appropriate exercise. Cold water baths or cold water rubs are also helpful methods for assisting in the treatment.

A Casual Discussion on Lung Disease 213

— Physician Shen Zhaoquan

1. No Medicine Exists Today to Directly Kill Tuberculosis Bacteria

Today, the lung remedies sold on the market are numerous and too many to list. Those advertised with exaggerated claims of efficacy in newspapers and magazines all prove to be illusions upon clinical experimentation, ultimately revealing their complete ineffectiveness. However, many lung disease sufferers are misled by these claims, delaying proper treatment and leading themselves to a hopeless situation.

The cause of pulmonary tuberculosis is the tubercle bacillus, a fact widely known by those with some scientific knowledge. This bacterium is extremely resistant, and no medicine can easily eradicate it. Despite rapid advancements in modern medicine, an effective drug that can directly kill the tubercle bacillus has yet to be discovered. Our principle in treating tuberculosis is to enhance the body’s resistance, indirectly leading to recovery, rather than directly killing the bacteria.

Although many agents can directly kill tubercle bacilli in laboratory test tubes, they all possess intense toxicity. If used in the human body, they would cause immense harm before eradicating the bacteria. Moreover, medications, whether taken orally or injected, must circulate through blood vessels throughout the body to reach the lesions to be effective. However, tuberculosis lesions are located in a corner of the lung tissue where no blood vessels exist. Therefore, even if a safe bactericidal drug existed, its effectiveness could not be manifested. In other words, the site of bacterial proliferation is unreachable by drugs. Thus, the unreliability of such drugs acting on tubercle bacilli within the body can be understood.

2. Using Endocrine Preparations as Adjunctive Therapy Can Shorten the Recovery Process

Patients with pulmonary tuberculosis often suffer from neurasthenia and metabolic disorders, which greatly weaken their resistance and hinder recovery. From my clinical experience, in addition to general fundamental therapies for treating lung disease, I also use the endocrine preparation "Wille Tonic" for patients to take orally. (This product is made from the essence extracted from the youth glands of animals.) After taking it for ten or more days, patients feel mentally refreshed, their appetite improves, the vitality of their body's cells is restored, the dwindling life functions are recovered, and the phenomenon of premature aging is stopped. As a result, natural resistance increases, leading to improved disease conditions and a shortened recovery process. Furthermore, lung disease patients often experience nocturnal emissions, making "Wille Tonic" even more appropriate.

3. Calcium and Pulmonary Tuberculosis

Calcium, whose component is lime, functions to increase the amount of lime in the blood, depositing it in the lesions to harden them, promote scar formation, and prevent their spread. It also inhibits inflammation and has a strong clotting power, preventing hemoptysis. For this reason, despite the continuous emergence of new drugs, the application of calcium has not diminished.

To introduce large amounts of calcium into the patient's body, intravenous injection is necessary. Although oral administration can introduce a large amount each time, it cannot be fully absorbed and is mostly excreted, yielding little effect. Therefore, among the various calcium preparations sold on the market, injections are effective, while oral administration is ineffective. If patients purchase them for oral consumption, it is merely a waste of money.

Calcium injections should be given once daily, gradually increasing the dosage. Mild cases may see results after fifty to sixty injections. Severe cases may not see results without more than a hundred injections. Furthermore, the injection procedure is quite difficult and should be performed by a skilled physician.

(Our hospital has an economical lung treatment program, covering the cost of injections until recovery for only sixty yuan.)

4. Strenuous Exercise for Lung Disease Patients is Equivalent to Suicide

Most lung disease patients are thin and emaciated. It is commonly said that exercise can strengthen the body and develop muscles. Therefore, patients, without considering the consequences, engage in exercise, leading to a deepening of the disease and making it incurable. It is important to realize that exercise for fitness is suitable for healthy individuals, but not for patients. Because the lungs of lung disease patients are already damaged (i.e., tuberculosis), the goal is to allow cells to surround the affected area and promote scarring for healing. Engaging in exercise accelerates blood circulation and deepens lung respiration, making the tuberculosis lesions prone to rupture and preventing scar formation. At the same time, it gives the tubercle bacilli (i.e., tuberculosis bacteria) an opportunity to spread. It is truly regrettable. Therefore, I earnestly and loudly proclaim to everyone: "Lung disease patients must rest quietly and avoid exercise at all costs. Exercise is suicide!"

5. Scarring of Lung Lesions is a Sign of Tuberculosis Healing

The physiological and anatomical phenomenon of lung disease healing is the encapsulation of tuberculosis lesions in the lungs by the body's cells and tissues, forming scars. As a result, all symptoms subside, and health is restored. Therefore, those with strong physical fitness have sufficient resistance, enabling cells to effectively surround the affected area, forming scars and leading to recovery. Our fundamental principle in treating tuberculosis is based on this.

Modern scholars consider drug treatment for tuberculosis to be unreliable and have harmful and toxic effects on the body, not a safe treatment method. Therefore, based on the aforementioned principle of scarring for healing, modern scholars have pioneered a new approach: organ therapy (i.e., using preparations made from animal lungs and spleens) for tuberculosis, which has shown remarkable effectiveness.

The earliest inventor of this organ preparation is "Phith Weal," which is widely sold on the market. This product is the pioneer of organ therapy for tuberculosis and can be called a world-exclusive holy medicine for lung treatment.

The ingredients contained in "Phith Weal" are hormones harmoniously extracted and produced from the fresh lungs, spleens, livers, testicles, and other organs of mammals. In addition, it contains tonic lecithin (also known as lipids) and valuable medications for cough suppression and phlegm reduction. Patients can achieve the effects of taking more than ten types of medications simultaneously by using this one medicine ("Phith Weal").

After taking it, tuberculosis patients experience increased appetite, sound sleep, elimination of night sweats, increased weight, mental vitality, a rosy complexion, reduced or eliminated fever, thinned sputum, reduced or completely stopped coughing.

Scientifically speaking, after ingestion, the active ingredients of these organ preparations are absorbed into the blood from the stomach, circulate throughout the body, and have a direct effect on the lungs. They stimulate the weakened tissues in the lesions, maintaining the harmony of their functions, promoting tissue regeneration, and filling in their defects (repairing cavities). At the same time, they build a solid connective tissue wall around the lesions, hardening them, forming scars, and completely encapsulating the evil tubercle bacilli, cutting off their food supply, and causing them to die. This agent also promotes blood coagulation, significantly preventing hemoptysis. This has been proven by physicians in various countries.

Recently, I used "Phith Weal" to treat one hundred lung disease patients, and the recovery rate was over 85%, setting a new record for modern tuberculosis treatment. Tidbits 214

— (Ji Yijie)

Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, the leader of the Fascist Party, once told his party members: "In life, one must be courageous and forge ahead. One cannot be overly cautious and hesitant in everything. As a leader, I must lead by example and live amidst danger, without evading it." He also said, "If I retreat, kill me. If I advance, follow me. If I die, avenge me." From these words, one can understand his character.

Mussolini has an unwavering ambition and a spirit of self-improvement. He despises those who live in a drunken stupor, wasting money and time. While serving as the government's prime minister and the party's leader, he could have lived a life of ease and arrogance. However, he maintained a very strict private life. Apart from obligatory dinners, he never set foot in theaters or aristocratic cafes. Therefore, he moved the entire ancient Roman nation and inspired the people of Italy, leading to today's vibrant and energetic Italy.

The Eccentric Old Man 215

— Tang Kuangsong

According to my friend Mr. Chen, his great-uncle had some interesting habits. After hearing about them, I felt they met the criteria of an eccentric and I'm writing them down as follows:

The old man lived to be seventy-nine years old, which is not a short lifespan. According to him, he was able to live long because he never washed his body. One bath, and all the original qi is lost. External colds take the opportunity to invade, easily causing illness. When people have a balanced qi, it naturally circulates. After bathing, the body is tired and exhausted, and the internal organs become deficient. It is not a way to maintain good health. Therefore, besides the three "exercises" that Chinese people must do, he never immersed his body in water. When people argued with him, he would stroke his beard and say with smug satisfaction, using himself as an example: "Look at me, you little kids, learn from me!"

Once the Mid-Autumn Festival passed, he would put on a blue cotton robe and wear it until the summer solstice of the following year, when he would switch to a summer linen gown that he had worn for decades, as if his year only had winter and summer.

Old people have weakening heart blood and do not like to sleep at night. At the same time, they easily get hungry during the long nights. So, he put peanut candies next to his pillow, and rats made a comfortable nest in his bed. But he didn’t care at all. Having nothing to do at night, he would take out the silver dollars he had saved throughout his life from the cellar and count them one by one, almost every night. Later, someone replaced his silver dollars with fakes, but he did not know at all.

Three days before his death, he bought all kinds of fireworks and set them off continuously at the door for three days and nights. When he died, people said he had ascended to heaven.

Supplement to the Jade Mountain Cottage 216

— Xu Yunqiu

My previous research on the Jade Mountain Cottage was not comprehensive, so I am supplementing it.

During the late Yuan Dynasty, Gu Aying lived amidst the turmoil of war but excelled in garden and pavilion construction. Day and night, he hosted high-ranking and talented individuals, setting up wine and composing poetry, enjoying endless celebrations, almost forgetting that it was a time of great unrest. Famous scholars of the time, such as Yang Lianfu, Ni Yunlin, and Ke Jiusi, and dozens of others joined his society. (Dong Chao's Dong Gao Miscellaneous Records)

The Jade Mountain Gathering took place in February of the Zhi Zheng Wuzi year. Zhongying was not yet forty years old, and at that time, the world had been peaceful for a long time. The cottage was famous in Suzhou. Scholars from all over the country who passed through Suzhou would inquire about the cottage, and Zhongying generously used his wealth to gather guests, enjoying the company of famous figures and poets, indulging in literary and wine gatherings almost every day. The elegance and literary talent of these gatherings truly illuminated the ages. However, in November of that year, Fang Guozhen's troops rose up in Taizhou. From then on, Liu Futong, Xu Shouhui, Chen Youliang, and Zhang Shicheng, among others, waged war, causing chaos. By the Bing Shen year, when Shicheng entered Wu, the cottage was almost destroyed by the army, and people fled in disarray, with no more joy as before. (Xingmei Poetry Talk)

There were twenty-four pavilions and halls in Zhongying's Jade Mountain Cottage. The plaques and scrolls were inscribed by famous officials, senior scholars, and elegant individuals, who expressed their admiration for Zhongying through their poems and calligraphy. Zhongying cherished them more than antiques. In the Guisi year, the thirteenth year of the Zhi Zheng era, Zhang Shicheng raised troops in Taizhou, disrupting the three Wus. In the Bing Shen year, troops entered the cottage in the first month, and the paintings and calligraphy were all taken away. In the second month, Zhang Shicheng's troops entered Pingjiang. In the fourth month, hundreds of soldiers suddenly arrived with weapons, urgently seeking Zhongying. At that time, Zhongying was still seeking refuge on a boat, thus escaping. When he returned to the cottage, all the scrolls had been taken. One day, Commander Feng Bingzhong visited and told Shenying: "Your family's poetry scrolls were taken away by the soldiers. I knew that you valued them, so I retrieved them all for you and will return them tomorrow." In a few days, he brought back more than seventy scrolls stored in boxes to the cottage. When inspecting the scrolls from the pavilions and halls, only the scrolls from the Willow Pond, Crimson Snow, and Green Waves were missing. Zhongying, along with Yuan Ziying and Ma Mengzhao, searched for them separately. Zhongying also recorded the dates of gaining and losing them. (Collection of Jade Mountain Cottage) (Xingmei Poetry Talk)

The Simmons Story 218

— He Jiale

Because she was too fat, people called her "Simmons."

"Simmons" is the specific name for a type of Western-style bed: this thing is soft and comfortable, and if it is under someone's body, how can it not be intoxicating?

For this reason, all of us male colleagues secretly dedicated this elegant name to our fat and fleshy girl.

Unfortunately, our Miss Simmons lacks common sense: she does not understand the meaning of "Simmons": when we discovered this weakness; we male colleagues became even wilder and more absurd; before, we said it behind her back, but now it is different, to her face:

"Miss Simmons!"

"What are you saying?" she asked:

"Um—this is a respectful address for pretty ladies!"

She smiled knowingly—she fell for our trick!

From then on: the fun began: everyone called her "Simmons" in a serious and seemingly intimate tone!

Until now, Miss Simmons is still in the dark about our deception.

Anecdotes about Sun Chuanfang 220

— Aimei

Ten years ago, he was known as the "United Commander of Five Provinces," awe-inspiring for a time. After his defeat, he devoted himself to Buddhism, repenting for his killings. Recently, Sun Chuanfang was assassinated in Tianjin's Buddhist Layman's Forest by Shi Jianqiao, a woman claiming to be avenging her father. This reminds me of some old stories about him that I can share with readers.

In the early summer of 1926, I had a brief encounter with Sun. At that time, I was only thirteen years old, studying at Bao Ying Si Bu Elementary School, when he retreated to northern Jiangsu. A few days earlier, a battalion of defeated soldiers retreated, barging into our school and disrupting the classrooms. Teachers retreated, and students scattered in chaos. As a result, the school suspended classes and became a camp for soldiers. A few days later, the United Commander's imperial entourage (?) arrived. I remember that the county magistrate, named Xie Ying, style name Shitong, busily led all civil and military officials to hold a welcome meeting, specifically calling for teachers and students from various schools to participate. Therefore, I also got to see his honorable face, truly a great honor. The United Commander kindly gave us some encouraging instructions and even rewarded us with some money, which was very warm and touching. Unfortunately, we couldn't continue our studies at the time, which was also thanks to the United Commander!

In the evening, after returning home from the meeting, we couldn't help but chat about the day's events. This sparked my father's conversation, and he told a widely known story of injustice, that is, a past event of Sun: "During the Qi-Lu War, Sun began to prosper. He started to worry about his high position and wanted to eliminate dissidents. He sent countless plainclothes detectives, densely distributed in various ports, to detect and arrest the so-called rebels. At that time, there was a small business owner surnamed Chen in Zhenjiang. Because there was discord between his wife and mother-in-law, he couldn't stand the pressure from both sides, so he left home and ran away to Shanghai, planning to make a living on his own. However, after staying for half a month, he still couldn't find a job, and the money he had brought was running out. He was always stuck in the hotel, inevitably sighing. Coincidentally, a detective lived in the room next door. Because he couldn't catch any reactionaries, he was also frowning. He had heard the sighing from the neighboring room for three days in a row and suddenly had an idea. He went over to get to know the man surnamed Chen, and they hit it off, becoming friends. The man surnamed Chen was inexperienced and had no social knowledge. He couldn't help but reveal his background and intentions. The detective was even more delighted and used sweet words, claiming to be Sun's confidant, promising to recommend him for a job, which would definitely succeed. He flattered him, luring him to Nanjing. The man surnamed Chen couldn't refuse? The next day, the detective took out a paper package and a letter, both tightly sealed, and gave them to the man surnamed Chen, saying: 'This letter is my recommendation letter. The paper package contains Sun's documents. He had asked me for it. Please take them all to him and present them to the United Commander!' He put the man surnamed Chen on the train. After the train left, he immediately sent a telegram to Sun, saying: 'A rebel, Chen, is taking the train to the province at a certain time, and will arrive at a certain time. Please send troops to the station to arrest him immediately.' When the man surnamed Chen arrived at the station, he saw a team of soldiers rushing onto the train. They asked: 'Who is Mr. Chen?' He thought they were there to welcome him, so he was overjoyed and quickly stepped forward to admit it. The soldiers immediately changed their faces, tied him up, and searched his luggage, finding the letter and the paper package. When they opened them, they were all reactionary documents, and the letter was the detective's report of his success to the United Commander. Without giving him a chance to explain, they grabbed him like a swallow and took him to Yaostreet, where he was executed by firing squad. It turned out that Sun had ordered them: 'I am busy and don't have time to interrogate. If you don't find any evidence, just detain him for now. If the evidence is solid, then execute him first, and then report to me.' When the man surnamed Chen's family received the news, although they had connections in the province, they could have rescued him, but how could they have made it in time? All they could do was go to the province and claim a wronged body. When my father told the story, he remembered the names of the deceased and his family, as well as the name of the wood shop. But now, after so long, I have forgotten them, so I can only record the events."

Now, Sun is dead. As for his life's rights and wrongs, merits and demerits, history will judge them. I don't need to say too much. But thinking of the "changing stars and shifting objects, ten years of vicissitudes," I can't help but feel: "Where is the hero of the world now?"

Notes on What I Saw 221

— (Yangtze River)

Walking through the alley on Jiaozhou Road, Ri Xin Village, past the Shen Guo football field, I saw the wicked ingenuity of some wild children again.

Two children, eleven or twelve years old, were pulling two bamboo fence poles away, while a child of eight or nine was struggling to pull because he was too weak.

The gap in the fence was already quite large. Dogs could enter and exit freely. If people were willing to humble themselves, they could also go in and out freely by bending over. But in the wild children's basket, all that could be seen was a uniform collection of broken fence bamboo, which was enough to prove where the bamboo was going and where the small woodcutters' firewood came from.

As soon as the smallest child had pulled one stalk, he retreated into the opposite alley. Out of curiosity, I wanted to see their expressions, so I stood at the entrance of the alley without moving. Unexpectedly, the smallest child calmly said to me:

What? Do you want to come in? If you don't, I'm going to close the door.

Immediately, he closed half of the iron gate of the alley. I vaguely saw them doing the breaking work.

On the way, I thought that this is not only an educational problem but also a serious social problem.

Important Discoveries in Modern Medicine (Part 1) 222

— Xie Junshou

Science is advancing, changing with each passing day. The progress of new medicine is also advancing alongside the progress of science. Before the 15th century, European medicine was mired in philosophical medicine, engaging in mutual debates and divergent factions, much like the current state of traditional medicine in our country. The 15th and 16th centuries are called the Renaissance by historians. Scholars broke through the fallacies of tedious schools of thought, corrected the mistakes of the ancients, and added religious reforms. Epidemics were prevalent. Medical scientists cultivated a spirit of faithfully observing nature. The face of medicine underwent a change. By the 17th century, natural sciences such as astronomy, physics, mathematics, chemistry, and various sophisticated machines were developing and progressing daily. Medicine, under the influence of science, also showed significant progress. Many important medical inventions began in this century. Now, the important medical discoveries since the 17th century will be described below. It is hoped that those who are mindful of the progress of new medicine will be pleased to hear it.

Common Knowledge Q&A About Diseases 223

— Cheng Hanzhang

(Q) What is liver fluke disease?

(A) Liver fluke disease (Distenriasis hepates) is caused by a type of fluke (distoma) that parasitizes the liver.

(Q) How does one become infected with this parasite?

(A) The larvae of this parasite first parasitize aquatic organisms such as snails and crucian carp; people become infected after eating these.

(Q) What symptoms appear when people have this parasite in their liver?

(A) Normally it starts in the summer and autumn. You may feel an increased appetite, a feeling of fullness in the stomach, and sometimes diarrhea. The liver becomes enlarged and then later shrinks. The liver surface is smooth but without tenderness.

(Q) What do patients feel as the disease progresses?

(A) As the disease progresses, more severe diarrhea is seen. Because the parasite's irritation causes a large amount of bile to flow into the intestines. Lower limb edema, ascites, night blindness, etc. may occur. The spleen also becomes enlarged. In addition, anemia, epistaxis, hematemesis, and hematochezia may develop. As a result, the patient's whole body weakens and leads to death. Different from cirrhosis, edema of the skin is seen at the same time as ascites.

(Q) Does the disease always progress continuously?

(A) No. It is usually mild in winter and worsens in summer and autumn.

(Q) What disease should it be distinguished from?

(A) It should be distinguished from liver fragmentation disease. Simply check the stool for the presence of parasite eggs.

(Q) Is this disease dangerous?

(A) It is less dangerous to life; however, severe diarrhea or bleeding from various parts of the body is dangerous.

(Q) How is liver fluke disease treated?

(A) If people eat vegetables contaminated with dog tapeworm (Distomiasishepatescoccus), hydatid cysts may develop in the liver, with two types: unilocular and multilocular. So, liver hydatid cysts are caused by dog tapeworms parasitizing the liver.

(Q) What are the symptoms of unilocular liver hydatid cysts?

(A) If it occurs on the liver surface, an elastic, undulating mass will appear, moving with breathing. Although there are no symptoms such as anemia or cachexia, there are often many complications such as cyst suppuration and perforation into the gastrointestinal tract.

(Q) What are the symptoms of multilocular liver hydatid cysts?

(A) Rarely seen. The liver develops into a hard, solid tumor that does not undulate but is tender. Jaundice, ascites, splenomegaly, or gastrointestinal bleeding often develop.

(Q) Is this disease dangerous?

(A) Unilocular cysts are not very dangerous; multilocular cysts are dangerous.

(Q) How are liver hydatid cysts treated?

(A) Unilocular cysts can be treated with surgery; multilocular cysts cannot.

Common Sense Hygiene for Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eyes 226

— Tang Renjin

(71) Foreign Objects in the Ear

The condition of foreign objects in the ear refers to the presence of foreign objects in the external auditory canal. There are many types of foreign objects. For example, beans, beads, buttons, small shells, matchsticks, as well as mosquitoes, flies, lice, stink bugs, etc., can all enter the ear. There are two ways that foreign objects can enter: voluntary and involuntary. Children often play with beans, beads, buttons, etc., and put them into their ears themselves. Adults often have the habit of using matchsticks (as a substitute for ear picks) to scratch the external auditory canal, which often leads to breakage and entry into the ear. Both are voluntary entries. As for mosquitoes, flies, lice, stink bugs, etc., they mostly belong to involuntary entry. The symptoms caused by foreign objects entering the ear vary greatly. Some may enter the ear and have no symptoms even after several years. Others may damage the external auditory canal or eardrum, causing the patient to suddenly panic and feel frightened. Some may not have tinnitus, dizziness, hearing loss, etc. at first, but later develop these symptoms due to the entry of water. There are countless possibilities. Now, let's briefly describe the symptoms caused by each type of foreign object as follows:

(1) Beans—After children put beans into their ears themselves, there may be no symptoms. However, once water enters the ear (washing face or bathing), the beans will swell up upon contact with water and fill the ear, causing the child to suddenly feel tinnitus, dizziness, hearing loss, etc., attracting the parents' attention and seeking medical treatment.

(2) Beads, Buttons, Small Shells—These are mostly round and do not damage the external auditory canal or eardrum. They also do not swell up upon contact with water. Therefore, there are often no symptoms even after several years.

(3) Matchsticks—Matchsticks are mostly used to stop itching in the external auditory canal. Because people are eager to stop the itching, they will use great force. Therefore, there are two possible results. One is that the matchstick easily breaks and enters the ear, becoming a foreign object in the ear. The other is damage to the external auditory canal (most common) or even the eardrum, leading to external otitis or otitis media, causing sudden swelling, pain, pus discharge, and other suffering. This is something we have encountered many times.

(4) Mosquitoes, Flies, Bugs, Stink Bugs—The entry of these small creatures into the ear is entirely involuntary. Therefore, they constantly fly around and move within the ear, trying to get out. At this time, the patient feels something moving in the ear and thinks that it has already entered the brain, suddenly causing terror and panic. In fact, anatomically speaking, it is impossible for it to enter the brain.

Regarding the foreign objects mentioned above, do not try to remove them yourself or have them removed by barbers with no medical knowledge, as it can often backfire, pushing them further in or damaging the external auditory canal or middle ear, causing pain and danger. Therefore, it is imperative that a doctor examines the type, size, shape, and location of the foreign object in detail. Then, use ear drops, ear irrigation, or extraction methods accordingly. In some cases, surgery may even be required for the most appropriate treatment.

In the Midst of Tuberculosis Prevention, Our Understanding of Pulmonary Tuberculosis Should Be (Part 2) 227

— Zhong Zhihe

(3) Environment: Chinese people often like to live in large family groups, with dense populations and small, closely packed houses. The air is turbid and scarce. There is little outdoor exercise and no attention to hygiene. Public organizations, institutions, factories, schools, etc., lack sanitary facilities, weakening people's resistance and making them susceptible to the disease.

(4) Precautions: A. Spitting everywhere spreads germs. Recently, the Department of Pulmonary Tuberculosis of the First Hospital of the Chinese Red Cross Society conducted a field survey in a small vegetable market and other busy areas, collecting 100 sputum samples from the ground. 10% of the sputum contained tubercle bacilli. The actual number of TB cases is even higher than the aforementioned percentage. Chinese people often spit out sputum at will without examination, so there is a lot of tuberculosis. And B. Not washing hands before meals allows dust to transmit germs, unknowingly carrying tubercle bacilli into the mouth or respiratory tract.

(5) Cow's Milk: Among animals, cows are most likely to have tuberculosis. And the number of people drinking cow's milk is increasing. If cows are not examined and the milk from sick cows is given to people to drink, tuberculosis will often be transmitted to humans.

(6) Transmission: A. Talking to patients. B. Kissing. C. Sharing food without separate servings. D. Carelessly touching the patient's clothes, bedding, utensils, chopsticks, sputum cups, etc. For example, laborers, nurses, and doctors in hospitals are sometimes easily infected. E. According to a survey by the U.S. Public Health Service, postal workers who handle letters and stamps daily are infected by germs on the stamps. Approximately 1% of those who send 100 to 500 letters per day have tuberculosis. This is likely due to the common habit of moistening the back of stamps with saliva and sticking them on envelopes.

(7) Occupation: Those who work as machinists and laborers in trains, ships, and factories are constantly exposed to coal gas, making them prone to pulmonary tuberculosis. In addition, stone masons, miners, leather workers, etc., who inhale impurities are also susceptible to lung diseases. Also, those who sit still and rarely see the sun are prone to weakness and lung disease.

(8) Constitution: Those with a weak constitution are prone to pulmonary tuberculosis.

(9) Special: Those with febrile diseases and chronic diseases such as whooping cough, pleurisy, pneumonia, measles, and diabetes are susceptible to pulmonary tuberculosis.

(10) Local Conditions: Patients with scrofula, tuberculous lymphadenitis, etc., often develop pulmonary tuberculosis at the same time. (11) Tubercle bacillus (Bacillus tuberclb)

(4) Symptoms of Pulmonary Tuberculosis:

The symptoms of pulmonary tuberculosis can be summarized as follows: 1. Night cough and expectoration. 2. Hemoptysis (coughing up blood) accounts for approximately 60% to 80% of cases. 3. Night sweats. 4. Low-grade fever. Often felt in the afternoon or evening. 5. Cheek redness. 6. Decreased appetite and weight loss. 7. Chest pain. 8. Anemia and emaciation. 9. Irritability, etc. Recently, Peterdy of the United States has classified symptoms by cause, making them clearer. Here is a special record. A classification of the ordinary symptoms of pulmonary tuberculosis according to the following cause

The first category is due to blood toxicity and aging (1) Lack of endurance (Lock of eudulauec) (2) Fatigue and weakness. (3) Nerve instability (Nerve instability) (4) Digestive impairment. (5) Metabolic disturbances result in weight loss. (6) Pulse rate increases. (7) Night sweats. (8) Body temperature rises (9) Changes in blood.

The second category is caused by reflection. (1) Hoarseness. (2) Throat irritation. (3) Cough. (4) Digestive impairment. (5) Changes in blood circulation. (6) Chest and scapular pain. (7) Cheek redness. (8) Spasms of the muscles of the shoulder girdle. Spasms of the central tendon and diaphragmatic crura. (9) The movement of the affected side is reduced by traction. Local symptoms due to toxins and reflection

The third category is local symptoms caused by toxins and reflection. (1) Frequent colds and prolonged colds. (Tuberculous tracheobronchitis) (2) Hemoptysis. (3) Membranitis. (Tuberculosis of the pleura) (4) Cough.

Pain Relief Medicine (4) (2) 228

— Li Xing

The first local anesthetic discovered was cocaine. Cocaine is a compound analyzed from coca leaves. The Red Indians of Chile and Bolivia in South America have chewed coca leaves since ancient times to suppress hunger or remove fatigue or stimulate nerve excitement. The precursor to the discovery of cocaine was in 1860, when Wöhler, Niemann, and Lossen simultaneously pointed out that cocaine had the effect of numbing the tongue, but unfortunately, its importance was not realized. In 1880, the British Medical Council only recognized cocaine as a stimulant that could be used as a substitute for caffeine. In the same year, Anrep meticulously studied the various medicinal properties of cocaine. In 1884, Koller, an ophthalmologist in Vienna, tried the ordinary medicinal properties of cocaine. He recognized that the effect of cocaine numbing the tongue was an anesthetic effect. Because he was paying attention to ophthalmic anesthetics, he experimented with cocaine, first dripping cocaine solution into the eyes of livestock, and then experimenting on ophthalmic patients in the hospital. He found that cocaine was a powerful anesthetic. So he reported his discovery at the Ophthalmology Association. From this time on, cocaine local anesthetic was introduced to the world and became popular globally.

Although cocaine was available as a local anesthetic, it was not an ideal local anesthetic because it was prone to poisoning and had limited uses. Later scholars continued to study cocaine substitutes and discovered several better local anesthetics. Today, cocaine is gradually being used less and less, and in the near future, it will probably only remain a name in medical history.

The action of a local anesthetic is to locally numb the sensory nerves (or pain nerves). When the local nerve is numbed, it will not transmit the sensation of pain to the pain center in the brain when it is injured, so the injured area does not feel pain. For example, before a tooth extraction, an anesthetic is injected into the root of the tooth, numbing the nerves of the tooth and the nerves of the gums. This cannot transmit the sensation of pain to the brain, so you won't feel pain when the tooth is extracted. The reason for injecting an anesthetic for pain relief during local surgery is the same. If cocaine-like anesthetics are dropped on mucous membranes, such as in the nose or eyes, they can have a numbing effect. From this, it can be seen that local anesthetics are not some kind of miraculous effect.

Injecting a small amount of anesthetic has little effect on the body. On the one hand, it is more economical than taking drugs, and on the other hand, it is safer than taking drugs. The most common one currently used is novocaine, which has very low toxicity and is the most important injectable anesthetic. There are also various other anesthetics that are used for dripping, rubbing, or injecting, and their effects are much the same.

In addition to its numbing properties, cocaine also has anesthetic properties, its effect being stimulation followed by depression. Cocaine views cocaine as a stimulant, and its nature and action are similar to morphine, so cocaine is also one of the strictly prohibited drugs. Most cocaine offenders in the United States are black people, or prostitutes, or various criminal offenders. The responsibility for their crimes is partly due to the stimulating and confusing nerve action of cocaine. Doctors use cocaine in surgical operations to benefit patients, but ignorant people abuse injections to help excite and become arrogant, driving themselves to all kinds of evil, and actually making themselves a pest to mankind, so it is reasonable for them to be subject to the extreme punishment of the state. (End)

Common Knowledge Q&A About Teeth (11) (1) 229

— Lin Jianxian

(Question 58) Why should you pay the most attention to cavities?

(Answer) First, because they are most common. Second, because our teeth suffer the most damage from decay. Third, because in addition to causing local diseases, they can also cause various systemic diseases, greatly affecting health. Fourth, because this problem can be reduced if prevented early and stopped if treated promptly. So you should pay the most attention and study it more.

(Question 59) What has been thought to be the cause of cavities in our country?

(Answer) It was thought to be a visible, wriggling tooth worm in the mouth.

(Question 60) According to current medical discoveries, what is the cause of cavities?

(Answer) The most direct cause is acid in the mouth. It dissolves the collagen in the enamel and removes the lime in the teeth. Therefore, the part of the tooth that is eroded by acid will gradually soften and rot into a hole.

(Question 61) Where does the acid in the mouth come from?

(Answer) It is produced by the fermentation and acidification of food residue in the mouth, especially carbohydrates, such as starches and sugars, through the action of microorganisms.

(Question 62) Why is food residue in the mouth so easily fermented and acidified?

(Answer) All food fermentation requires suitable temperature, moisture, and enclosure, and there must be fermentation microorganisms present. (The yeast we use to make wine and vinegar is a type of fermentation bacteria. Milk will ferment and turn sour after being left for a long time, which is also the effect of fermentation bacteria.) Our mouths have a temperature, moisture, and darkness that are extremely suitable for fermentation. And there are many different types of microorganisms hidden. Therefore, food left in the mouth is extremely easily fermented and acidified. The mouth is like a manufacturing plant. In this plant, food is the raw material, microorganisms are the manufacturers, and acid is the manufactured product. If there is no raw material or no manufacturer, this harmful acid cannot be produced. Therefore, all three can be considered causes of cavities.

(Question 63) Is this fermentation microorganism a worm?

(Answer) It is not the tooth worm that we have always believed in. It is plant-based, not animal-based. And it is very small. Tens of millions of them can attach to one tooth. It is by no means visible to the naked eye. Furthermore, these microorganisms themselves do not damage the teeth. What is harmful is the lactic acid produced when they develop and reproduce.

(Question 64) Are there any other causes of cavities?

(Answer) In addition to the main cause mentioned above, there are many contributing factors that can induce cavities and help them progress. These contributing factors can be divided into systemic and local types.

(Question 65) How many local contributing factors are there?

(Answer) There are limited local contributing factors in the oral cavity: (1) Neglecting oral hygiene, being lazy about brushing teeth, and allowing food to accumulate. (2) Irregular tooth alignment, making them difficult to brush. (3) Hard tooth injuries, causing cracks (4) Eating more soft foods containing carbohydrates, such as rice, wheat, and sugar, and less coarse foods rich in fiber, such as vegetables and raw fruits. The former easily adheres to teeth, facilitating the progress of acidification, while the latter has the effect of grinding the teeth and natural cleaning.

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (7)(7) 230

— Hu Jiayan

(2) Lipoids: This is a method that has been popular for a long time. Even now, some people still use it. In fact, its therapeutic effect is only on the general condition of the patient, such as anemia and loss of appetite, which is not without improvement; it is also possible for the patient's weight to increase as a result. It has no direct effect on the lung disease itself. There are also quite a few preparations of this kind produced by pharmaceutical factories around the world; their contents are also different and each has its own characteristics. The ingredients include combinations of lecithin and glycerin, lipoids and "Ya Te Ling", and combinations of fatty lipids and wax. Its application is generally by injection into the human body; there are also a few made into ointments for external application.

(3) Drugs: This can also be called chemotherapy. We know that in the current treatment of pulmonary tuberculosis, there is absolutely no so-called specific drug that can directly kill tuberculosis bacteria without harming the human body. The clinical achievements mentioned here are undeniable; however, compared with the pharmacological basis and the truly effective drug, it is still far behind, which is beyond help. The characteristics and value of each of them are now described separately below:

(A) Gold Preparations: It has long been proven that gold preparations can kill tuberculosis bacteria, but direct use in treatment is not without harm to the human body; therefore, it is the expectation of every pharmaceutical expert and clinician to make gold preparations into non-toxic and effective drugs. But until now, it has not been completely successful. We must know that the current treatment principles for pulmonary tuberculosis are nothing more than two: one is to find ways to eliminate lesions and bacteria nests, and the other is to increase the patient's own vitality to resist the disease. Although gold preparations have the effect of directly killing bacteria, their purpose in clinical application is still biased towards the second method. Therefore, this type of newly produced preparation… although it has appeared, it is ultimately no more than a kind of stimulating therapy, and it is definitely not a specific drug: this should be clearly understood!

"Prohibiting Oil Transportation to Italy Almost Means War"? 231

— Fang Yin

Reuters, Rome, November 25: "If countries prohibit the transport of coal and oil to Italy, Italy will withdraw from the League of Nations. According to well-informed Italian sources: Mussolini regards cutting off the supply of coal and oil as a hostile act. If countries implement it, Italy will reconsider its position in the League of Nations. Mussolini accepted the implementation of financial and economic sanctions by the League of Nations under protest, but did not regard it as a hostile act. Now, if essential supplies are prohibited to Italy, making Italy's war in Abyssinia more difficult, it will inevitably cause a serious situation, which seems to cause dangerous reactions in Europe."

This time, the League of Nations, under the support of Britain and France—especially British imperialism, implemented unprecedentedly tough sanctions against Italy's war of aggression against Abyssinia. This move seems to have some sense of justice on the surface, but in reality, everyone knows that this is a head-on collision between British and Italian imperialism. However, we cannot deny that League of Nations member states such as the Soviet Union and small and weak nations have expressed their sympathy and assistance to Abyssinia in this sanction.

This sanction is undoubtedly a very serious threat to Italian ideologists. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has repeatedly protested and considered withdrawing from the League of Nations, and has resorted to concentrating domestic cash, restricting the export of goods, and reducing various consumptions…etc. to show how anxious and worried he is about coping with this sanction, in order to resolve the difficulties in the war of aggression against Abyssinia and the general situation. The most uncomfortable thing for Italy in this difficulty is naturally the prohibition of coal and oil transportation to Italy by various countries.

In modern war countries, coal and oil occupy a very important position. Prohibiting the transport of coal and oil to Italy is tantamount to making Italy lose an important link in the war of aggression against Abyssinia, and abandoning all the previous victories of Italy. And Italy itself is not a country that produces coal and oil. Since this threat is so significant, Italy cannot but seek to resist it; therefore, it is also undoubtedly that the European situation will "cause dangerous reactions" as a result.

The Italian ambassador to France visited Laval on the 23rd and declared: "Prohibiting oil to Italy almost means war." Now Mussolini further "regards cutting off the supply of coal and oil as a hostile act," which shows the impact of the oil embargo on the current European situation. If this situation really changes seriously as the telegrams convey, then the words of the Italian ambassador to France are enough to make us smell the gunpowder.

Foreigners 232

— Simon

Lying in a deep slumber at night, on that street lit by dim gas lamps, with a desolate medieval feel, the huge black shadow of the chapel lay on the street. This residential area of ​​the wandering Norman ethnic group is full of the decadent sense of noble dreams and the feeling of national subjugation!

The dilapidated houses, chewing on the breath of moss, looking at those ragged and resentful imperial Russian remnants who have lost their bright smiles, but living here is very suitable for quietness, the hustle and bustle of the city is completely isolated, shrouded in an atmosphere of boundless loneliness. Every day, except for the chapel knocking with fragmented mirror sounds, there are few vehicles passing by, only letting the gentle sun occupy the resting place.

That white-haired landlord still maintains the leisurely lifestyle he used to be unwilling to give up: getting up early to urge the servants to wash the stairs and dust off the ceiling. Then he went out and bought a bunch of fresh flowers, leisurely walked back, inserted them into the vase, then dragged out a broken rattan chair with its roots torn apart, sat on the stone steps outside the door to bask in the sun, and looked down, dreaming a shattered gorgeous dream there.

"Hello, Good morning"

Every time he glanced at me coming out, he always said this in not very fluent English, looking at me faintly with dull eyes.

This old foreign wanderer is wearing dirty and broken clothes. Like a beggar. But this is not what makes me annoying. What I hated from the beginning was living such a vague, homeless, gray existence, stubbornly clinging to the decadent gentleman's habits of the owning class and hypocritical petit bourgeois rituals. These poor people!

In the big house, sounds are rarely heard, and the floor is covered with thick felt, so even the footsteps of people walking are gone. Like an empty temple without anyone living in it. The landlord doesn't work and lives off the rent. He himself uses contemplation and memories to pass the time. He hardly leaves the house for weeks, seemingly forgetting the world and being forgotten by the world at the same time.

However, what surprised me was that one day I walked into the landlord's bedroom, and the splendid and dazzling decorations, noble objects, and artful arrangements were simply what only a bourgeois person could have. This magnificent impression that caught my eye made me almost unable to believe my vision. I looked at the owner's old and broken clothes again, which aroused a very contradictory feeling. The exiled people of the old Russian emperor were so unwilling to take off their brilliant and glorious robes. But the brilliant and glorious robes had been snatched away by the Bolshevik warriors. What would you rely on to snatch them back?

The familiar white Russian wandering girl with chestnut hair and blue eyes also retained the arrogant posture of the buried king. She also used rouge to restore her aging youth. Although the cheongsam had faded, she still put on a holed jacket, walking so slowly and gracefully, humming a well-rhythmed tune while walking. Even when cooking in the kitchen, she didn't forget to sing while doing it. They seemed to have become accustomed to a wandering life, without memories, without longing for their Russian homeland, without sorrow. But who will appreciate your beauty, your smiles, your songs, and who are they leaning towards? Is it going to the jazz music nightclub, throwing yourself into the arms of foreigners, and imprinting the lipstick on your lips on the high stiff collar of a drunken sailor?

So tomorrow's borscht and cigarettes are exchanged for the sale of one's own body.

But what about tomorrow's tomorrow? What about the day after tomorrow? Exiled girls from Siberia, now it is winter. Has the grand costume for winter been made? Where is the warm homeland? Who are the listeners who pour out songs of passionate love to you?

Daughter-in-Law 233

— Hu Weixiong

The young mistress wiped away her tears, and was about to get up and go downstairs to find out what was going on, when a loud and strange noise rang out in the next room again:

"I said it long ago, people from small families are small-minded, and nothing pleases them! Marrying a wife should mean marrying one from a declining family. Look, they've driven your son out the door. You old hag, see what else you have to say?"

Although it was the old couple scolding each other, the wife deliberately raised her voice so that the young mistress could hear it, which was true. The young master had been out for two days and hadn't returned home, and the young mistress had been crying for two whole days—she no longer had any hope for her husband, but the wife's indirect scolding, beating the dog by scolding the chicken, scolded the young mistress as worse than anything. From morning to night, downstairs, in the next room, she ranted as she pleased, like singing the news; when guests came to visit, the wife found an opponent and added fuel to the fire, treating it like a myth, repeating it over and over again, one hundred and ten times. The root of everything was that people from small families were small-minded, and nothing pleased them; while the faults of her own precious son were praised in reverse: —"People say that the temper of an only son is spoiled. My A-Xiang has no temper. Not to mention his filial piety to his parents, he was obedient in every way when that thing entered the door—if he was asked to come back earlier, he would even refuse the socializing with his friends; he would bring back big bags and small bags every day to please her. In this situation, a man has to socialize outside. He just came home a little late that day, and the day hadn't even dawned, and she cried and screamed, causing unrest in the whole house! Humph! When we were daughters-in-law, we didn't dare to breathe loudly, but she even scolded everything out! Think about it, I'm so old, and I've got a daughter-in-law to teach me, shameless thing, does she need a man to sleep with her every day to feel comfortable?"

The wife was sometimes unable to catch her breath and rubbed her chest repeatedly, but as soon as she turned around, she called out again and again like a printing machine. The old master still spoke publicly: "What's the point of yelling and making a fuss like this! A-Xiang is not a good thing either. He's only been married for two months, and he's already hooked up with Ah-Xiang, who was brought over as a maid by his wife's family. Now he's out there messing around with flowers and grass until late at night. It's reasonable for the new mistress to persuade him. The young couple haven't broken up, but you're helping in there…"

This added fuel to the fire, and all the words scolding the daughter-in-law were moved to the "old hag's" body. In the end, she even said that the old man had no good intentions and was helping the daughter-in-law to teach his wife.

For the past two days, the mansion was like a teahouse, with people singing the news and people listening to the news, which made the servants cover their mouths and laugh. Some even told everything to the alley.

The young mistress hadn't left her room for two whole days, nor had she eaten. Ah-Xiang was a maid who had come over with her mother's family, and because she had been hooked up by the young master, she didn't dare to see the mistress either. An old woman, who had raised the young master, brought tea and rice to the room to persuade the young mistress. She said in a low voice:

"The wife just has this temper, she takes advantage of the wind. None of the people here have been able to stay long. The young master also has the wife's temper. Although I raised him, I don't hide it from you, this temper is difficult to deal with! Mistress, don't be angry, eat a little rice, it's not worth it to get angry. A beautiful new mistress like you, if you persuade him well, the young master will always change his mind."

The young mistress nodded, but in fact she didn't hear a word. She felt that the people in this house were as terrible as demons, and she was a prisoner under the claws of the demons. Even Ah-Xiang, who was on her side, had been hooked by them. The young mistress glanced at the furniture in the bedroom. A picture of lotus flowers growing on the same stem was reflected in the dressing mirror opposite her. She pushed the old woman out, fell on the bed and cried, but she didn't dare to cry out loud.

She resented her own fate, resented her family's poverty, so many people came to be matchmakers, but she married such a husband. He had abandoned her after only two months, and her mother-in-law was an unreasonable tiger. She wanted to go home immediately and cry to her mother, but how did her mother teach her when she went back home: Now you are a daughter-in-law, which is different from being a young lady at home. You must obey your in-laws in everything, and the young couple must get along well. You can't be willful! Does being a daughter-in-law mean serving her masters like a slave? The young mistress asked herself. Although a sympathetic answer was ringing in her ears, when she looked up, the room was empty and only she was alone. The mother-in-law's iron voice rang out again in the next room

"...Humph! Eating the Lu family's food is not easy, dying of hunger is just like dying a dog. Can't the Lu family find a thing like this? If A-Xiang doesn't come back for a day, you're not allowed to send food in, did you hear that?"

Small Notes Before the Window 234

— Taro

(1) Small First Words

I always lie on this only small writing desk near the window, writing, writing... When I feel tired, I drink tea and smoke to stimulate my spirit, but there is a time when tea and cigarettes lose their effectiveness, I use my two withered hands to hold my throbbing head, and look at the unknown old tree in front of the window, to temporarily relieve my depressed chest.

When will I be allowed to leave this window, even if it is only for a second, as long as that second is facing the selfless front.

(2) Broken Biscuits

In the left corner of the table, there is a bag of broken biscuits with only half left...

When I carried the broken biscuits back "home," the child jumped up with joy and called me in a very affectionate tone:

"Daddy! Daddy!"

I smiled and looked at the child, only to see her little eyes like those of a hungry cat, staring at the bag of broken biscuits. She licked her lips and asked me:

"Daddy! What is this?"

"Biscuits!"

Seeing the child's poor and pitiful face, I felt an unspeakable bitterness in my heart. My wife also came closer to me. I sat down on the chair, and the child quickly climbed onto my lap. I trembled, no, my heart trembled! I opened the bag of broken biscuits. The child hurriedly put her little hand into the mouth of the paper bag and grabbed a handful of biscuits. She took a look, was stunned for a moment, and a look of doubt appeared on her face. She looked at me, and then stuffed the broken biscuits into her mouth. I picked out a big piece and handed it to my wife:

"You taste one too!"

My wife silently accepted what I gave her. When I picked up a piece and put it in my mouth myself, the child suddenly asked me:

"Daddy! Why are these biscuits broken?"

I stared blankly! I almost wanted to shout at the child.

"You, baby! Why are you asking me this!"

But I didn't shout at the child after all. I only said to the child gently.

"You eat!"

(3) Fallen Leaves

I can't lie down and write anymore. Tea and cigarettes have lost their effect of stimulating my spirit. I held my head and looked out the window. - The leaves on that old tree fell down with a gust of wind!

This situation may not be felt by others, but for me, I, I can't bear to watch it to the end! I closed my eyes tightly, and infinite grief enveloped my chest. God! I, I,...

I wake up in the middle of the night every time. Logically speaking, my tired body should sleep well at night! But on the contrary, I woke up, and I can't fall asleep anymore! Coughing that stings the lungs is incessant all night long. Sometimes it wakes up my wife. She opened her eyes sleepily, swayed her feet, and got out of bed to pour me a glass of hot water and asked me to drink it. When she saw me drinking the boiled water, my wife covered her face and cried! Fallen leaves, why do you have to fall in front of my eyes!

(4) Cod Liver Oil

Seeing the fallen leaves, I felt even more fear that my life was heading towards the path of annihilation. I didn't want to die so young. I wanted to live, because I had unfinished responsibilities.

Cod liver oil, the advertisement said: "...are all effective, and especially good at treating lungs..." With the money I earned with my own blood, I bought a bottle. - But now, that bottle of cod liver oil will be drunk up in less than a week! My wife glanced at it, secretly took some things out, and when she came back, she bought a bag of rice.

I pretended not to see anything and just looked at the few cod liver oil in the bottle.

I saw the fallen leaves in front of the window again.

Life (Continued) 235

— Ji Xuan

So, under the names of "gambling house" and "boss," Ah Lin's heart gradually beat faster. He had set up a gambling house in the "Zhixuanju" teahouse on the street for his friends to "play" mahjong, poker, pai gow... It wasn't a day or two! Ah Lin had some "friendships" among the brothers of a group of "idlers," which everyone knew! Relying on this "gambling house," he had already made a lot of money from the nearby workers, and he had even taken a concubine. But he made friends on the "brother" level, and he had a "small axe" to "protect" his gambling house!

Facing this scene, he laughed loudly: "Friend, what do I owe you? Is that a 'gambling debt'? Haha, great, great, you report it to the bureau and ask people to arrest me, you go to the government to sue me, that's a 'gambling debt', isn't it?"

Snake-like venomous words hit Wang Da's dazed heart. Thinking of more than a year of unemployment, thinking of the many money lost (now, it has become a debt with heavy interest), thinking of tomorrow's life, he was stunned; a burst of heat rushed up from his heart, and he suddenly became clear, and suddenly grabbed Ah Lin's collar, and pulled this huge body out of the door like an ox and pounced on him.

"The money I lost! You liar! You...robber!"

The two shadows twisted together, scolding, pouncing, and beating, carrying the hatred used to deal with the flesh of life, carrying the inferior wine that had just been poured into their stomachs, and carrying the troubles of life these days, Wang Da smashed Ah Lin like crazy, and Ah Lin reached out to touch the small axe inserted in his waistband, but it was gone.

The noise spread, and on the dark street, three shadows ran over! They beat Wang Da, who was red-eyed, like wild beasts... He kept scolding: "You liar! You blood-sucking ghost!"... Finally, one person took an axe and slashed hard at Da's shoulder!

A strange cry rose in the dark night, and Wang Da's body relaxed. Three axes fell like two points and one line. Finally, blood flowed out like water, and the person was soaked in it.

Quietly, the three "brothers" slipped away from the darkness again. Ah Lin said to them with injuries, "Also let people know our interests... If you have any ideas, we'll talk about it tomorrow. If there's anything wrong? I'll protect the gambling house, I will!"

Everything returned to silence. The street lights shone on a pile of flesh and blood lying on the asphalt road. Now, he no longer had to worry about tomorrow's life...because he no longer had a tomorrow's life.
