Afterthoughts 242

The inaugural issue of "Zhou Bo" was published yesterday (i.e., in front of the Shanghai Commercial News Tofu Shop). The content is quite exciting. Chen Yaoting respectfully dedicates a poem to Bao Xuexue, "Mutual Understanding." Although the author states that there is no need to overthink and suspect, it is expected that there will be many people who will put their minds to it. Special introduction (Editor)

Miss Zhang Suzhen, director of the Ming Mei Troupe, went to Ningbo on the 22nd to perform. It is said that the price of her selling her thighs every day is five silver dollars.

Miss Chun Mei's mouth is indeed larger than that of ordinary people.

Miss Tao Tao has recently changed her name to Li Ling.

Mr. Ma Xingtao, the violinist of the Rose Troupe, plays the piano differently from others, actually using his right hand for harmony. It is truly rare.

Miss Lingling is currently studying at He'an Primary School on Xinzha Road. When playing, she often blurts out the phrase "Tell the teacher."

Miss Li Ya has recently been suffering from eye disease and has not yet recovered.

Mr. Xu Mingyi, the former president of Baijia Society, said that Yao Ping is the best pianist in the entire Shanghai broadcasting industry.

Mr. Xu Qi, the former president of Qiyin Society, has recently been diligently exploring Miss Liying's past history. It is said that he will write a biography of Miss Liying in tens of thousands of words. (Above by Mengying)

The second issue of "Feng Ming Ji," published by Feng Ming Advertising Agency, is about to be published. The content is richer and more exciting than the first issue. All kinds of noble recreational works are classified and categorized, making it a grand spectacle. It is also said that during the pre-order period, each copy is half-price, actually collecting three cents. Those from all walks of life who wish to request a copy should send a letter to Mr. Yuan Fengju, the chief editor of the book, at Feng Ming Advertising Agency on the fifth floor of the Great World, and it will be sent to them.

Movie News

Star Anecdotes 243

(1) The large set of Xu Ziyuan's villa in Qingdao for "Peach Blossoms After the Calamity," written by Hong Shen and directed by Zhang Shichuan, has been under construction for three weeks and has not yet been completed, which shows its greatness. The pavilions, terraces, flowers, and trees are luxuriant. It is estimated that there will be as many as twenty-one scenes in this part of the play.

(2) The sound photography studio of the Star General Factory has been actively underway in recent days, and it is expected to be completed by the end of the lunar year.

(3) Ye Qiuxin and Wang Zhengxin, the leading actors of "Love Letter," and others have recently been shooting outdoor scenes at the General Factory, wearing thin summer costumes, which can be said to be the ultimate sacrifice. Someone asked how it tasted after the filming? They replied: We know it ourselves.

(4) When filming at the entrance of the alley for "Spring Flowers," Old Gao played the role of a down-and-out person, wearing a broken Western suit bought from the Wusong Foreign Firm for one dollar and two cents.

(5) Because Hu Die is on vacation during her honeymoon, the filming of her scenes in "Brothers" has been temporarily put on hold, and Zhu Qiuhen's scenes will be filmed first.

Recent Announcement from the Shanghai Drama and Film Research Institute 244

The Shanghai Drama and Film Research Institute at Jiangwan Road Park Fang officially started classes on the 27th of this month. All professors arrived on time to teach, and the students were also very orderly. For the purpose of conducting extracurricular joint research, the students of the institute established a student association on the 29th and organized various research groups, such as the literary and art research group, etc. The school hired experts and celebrities to be responsible for guidance, and there are academic lectures every week, creating a very prosperous atmosphere.

"Heroes of the Times" in This Newspaper's Front Door Twenty Years Ago 245

New Contributions to Analyzing the Reasons for the Decline of Industry and Commerce in the Midst of the Economic Downturn 246

A Wake-Up Call to Expose the Causes of Decline A Morning Bell to Awaken Self-Reliance

Since the European economic panic spread to China, the phenomenon of economic downturn in Shanghai has become increasingly serious. Factories and shops have closed down one after another. Enthusiastic people are all anxious and racking their brains to find ways to save the situation. Yi Hua Film Company specially produced the play "Heroes of the Times" for this purpose. The play has a very clear description of the reasons for the decline of commerce and industry, especially the oppression of national capital by international capital, which can be thought-provoking. It is a wake-up call to dissect the reasons for the decline of commerce and industry, and it is enough to awaken the self-reliance of all sectors of society. It is now said that the film will be released soon at the Jincheng Grand Theater, and all industrial and commercial sectors unanimously praise the company for being able to make good use of film propaganda methods to do its best to appeal for the sake of industry and commerce.

Silver Miscellany 247

— Zhi Er

The Shanghai Tianyi Film Company's advertisement for recruiting actresses has the following conditions: (1) Age 18 to 22 years old, (2) Good-looking and beautiful, (3) Junior high school education, (4) Fluent Mandarin, (5) Height about four and a half feet, (6) Healthy physique, (7) Must have parental consent. An additional condition is that those from other places should not apply.

Since Mr. Shao Zuiweng went south to shoot Cantonese white mythological films, the Shanghai factory has long been empty. "Sea Burial" and "Mother" have also not sold well, so there is talk of sending Gao Tianqi to Hong Kong (of course, still to be in charge of publicity). Now, the Shanghai side has suddenly posted an advertisement for recruiting actresses, which is puzzling. Is it a whim of Zuiweng, or a consistent policy of "advertising gimmick"?

In terms of the conditions for recruiting actresses, it also feels contrary to our movie queen Ms. Chen Yumei. Does Mr. Shao, one of the world's three major directors, really feel that his wife is rotten wood that cannot be carved, and wants to promote new talents?

In the sound of "Communication by Telegram," the poet Miss Zhang Zhiyun was discovered again. Please see yesterday's Times for her great work. (External Historian, please note that this is a bit of free advertising.)

The editor of "Camera" has changed, and the new "Shaker" is "Idle Talk on Horseback" Tang Yu.
